Section 41.25 , subsection (3) , paragraph (c)  of the Canadian "Copyright Act" states:
>     41.25 (3)  A notice of claimed infringement shall not contain
>         (c)  a reference, including by way of hyperlink, to such an offer, request or demand; and

Section 41.25 , subsection (3) , paragraph (d)  of the Canadian "Copyright Act" states:
>     41.25 (3)  A notice of claimed infringement shall not contain
>         (d)  any other information that may be prescribed by regulation.


Section 41.26  : Provisions Respecting Providers of Network Services or Information Location Tools / Obligations related to notice
----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

Section 41.26 , subsection (1) , paragraph (a)  of the Canadian "Copyright Act" states:
>     41.26 (1)  A person described in paragraph 41.25(1)(a) or (b) who receives a notice of claimed infringement that complies with subsections 41.25(2) and (3) shall, on being paid any fee that the person has lawfully charged for doing so,
>         (a)  as soon as feasible forward the notice electronically to the person to whom the electronic location identified by the location data specified in the notice belongs and inform the claimant of its forwarding or, if applicable, of the reason why it was not possible to forward it; and

Section 41.26 , subsection (1) , paragraph (b)  of the Canadian "Copyright Act" states:
>     41.26 (1)  A person described in paragraph 41.25(1)(a) or (b) who receives a notice of claimed infringement that complies with subsections 41.25(2) and (3) shall, on being paid any fee that the person has lawfully charged for doing so,
>         (b)  retain records that will allow the identity of the person to whom the electronic location belongs to be determined, and do so for six months beginning on the day on which the notice of claimed infringement is received or, if the claimant commences proceedings relating to the claimed infringement and so notifies the person before the end of those six months, for one year after the day on which the person receives the notice of claimed infringement.

Section 41.26 , subsection (2)  of the Canadian "Copyright Act" states:
>     41.26 (2)  The Minister may, by regulation, fix the maximum fee that a person may charge for performing his or her obligations under subsection (1). If no maximum is fixed by regulation, the person may not charge any amount under that subsection.

Section 41.26 , subsection (3)  of the Canadian "Copyright Act" states:
>     41.26 (3)  A claimant’s only remedy against a person who fails to perform his or her obligations under subsection (1) is statutory damages in an amount that the court considers just, but not less than $5,000 and not more than $10,000.

Section 41.26 , subsection (4)  of the Canadian "Copyright Act" states:
>     41.26 (4)  The Governor in Council may, by regulation, increase or decrease the minimum or maximum amount of statutory damages set out in subsection (3).


Section 41.27  : Provisions Respecting Providers of Network Services or Information Location Tools / Injunctive relief only — providers of information location tools
---------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

Section 41.27 , subsection (1)  of the Canadian "Copyright Act" states:
>     41.27 (1)  In any proceedings for infringement of copyright, the owner of the copyright in a work or other subject-matter is not entitled to any remedy other than an injunction against a provider of an information location tool that is found to have infringed copyright by making a reproduction of the work or other subject-matter or by communicating that reproduction to the public by telecommunication.

Section 41.27 , subsection (2) , paragraph (a)  of the Canadian "Copyright Act" states:
>     41.27 (2)  Subsection (1) applies only if the provider, in respect of the work or other subject-matter,
>         (a)  makes and caches, or does any act similar to caching, the reproduction in an automated manner for the purpose of providing the information location tool;

Section 41.27 , subsection (2) , paragraph (b)  of the Canadian "Copyright Act" states:
>     41.27 (2)  Subsection (1) applies only if the provider, in respect of the work or other subject-matter,
>         (b)  communicates that reproduction to the public by telecommunication for the purpose of providing the information that has been located by the information location tool;

Section 41.27 , subsection (2) , paragraph (c)  of the Canadian "Copyright Act" states:
>     41.27 (2)  Subsection (1) applies only if the provider, in respect of the work or other subject-matter,
>         (c)  does not modify the reproduction, other than for technical reasons;

Section 41.27 , subsection (2) , paragraph (d)  of the Canadian "Copyright Act" states:
>     41.27 (2)  Subsection (1) applies only if the provider, in respect of the work or other subject-matter,
>         (d)  complies with any conditions relating to the making or caching, or doing of any act similar to caching, of reproductions of the work or other subject-matter, or to the communication of the reproductions to the public by telecommunication, that were specified in a manner consistent with industry practice by whoever made the work or other subject-matter available through the Internet or another digital network and that lend themselves to automated reading and execution; and

Section 41.27 , subsection (2) , paragraph (e)  of the Canadian "Copyright Act" states:
>     41.27 (2)  Subsection (1) applies only if the provider, in respect of the work or other subject-matter,
>         (e)  does not interfere with the use of technology that is lawful and consistent with industry practice in order to obtain data on the use of the work or other subject-matter.

Section 41.27 , subsection (3)  of the Canadian "Copyright Act" states:
>     41.27 (3)  If the provider receives a notice of claimed infringement, relating to a work or other subject-matter, that complies with subsections 41.25(2) and (3) after the work or other subject-matter has been removed from the electronic location set out in the notice, then subsection (1) applies, with respect to reproductions made from that electronic location, only to infringements that occurred before the day that is 30 days — or the period that may be prescribed by regulation — after the day on which the provider receives the notice.

Section 41.27 , subsection (4)  of the Canadian "Copyright Act" states:
>     41.27 (4)  Subsection (1) does not apply to the provision of the information location tool if the provision of that tool constitutes an infringement of copyright under subsection 27(2.3).

Section 41.27 , subsection (4.1) , paragraph (a)  of the Canadian "Copyright Act" states:
>     41.27 (4.1)  If it grants an injunction as set out in subsection (1), the court shall, among any other relevant factors, consider the following in establishing the terms of the injunction:
>         (a)  the harm likely to be suffered by the copyright owner if steps are not taken to prevent or restrain the infringement; and

Section 41.27 , subsection (4.1) , paragraph (b)  of the Canadian "Copyright Act" states:
>     41.27 (4.1)  If it grants an injunction as set out in subsection (1), the court shall, among any other relevant factors, consider the following in establishing the terms of the injunction:
>         (b)  the burden imposed on the provider and on the operation of the information location tool, including
>            (i)  the aggregate effect of the injunction and any injunctions from other proceedings,
>            (ii)  whether implementing the injunction would be technically feasible and effective in addressing the infringement,
>            (iii)  whether implementing the injunction would interfere with the use of the information location tool for non-infringing acts, and
>            (iv)  the availability of less burdensome and comparably effective means of preventing or restraining the infringement.

Section 41.27 , subsection (4.2)  of the Canadian "Copyright Act" states:
>     41.27 (4.2)  A court is not permitted to grant an injunction under section 39.1 against a provider who is the subject of an injunction set out in subsection (1).

Section 41.27 , subsection (5)  of the Canadian "Copyright Act" states:
>     41.27 (5)  In this section, information location tool means any tool that makes it possible to locate information that is available through the Internet or another digital network.


Section 42  : Criminal Remedies / Offences
------------------------------------------

Section 42 , subsection (1) , paragraph (a)  of the Canadian "Copyright Act" states:
>     42 (1)  Every person commits an offence who knowingly
>         (a)  makes for sale or rental an infringing copy of a work or other subject-matter in which copyright subsists;

Section 42 , subsection (1) , paragraph (b)  of the Canadian "Copyright Act" states:
>     42 (1)  Every person commits an offence who knowingly
>         (b)  sells or rents out, or by way of trade exposes or offers for sale or rental, an infringing copy of a work or other subject-matter in which copyright subsists;

Section 42 , subsection (1) , paragraph (c)  of the Canadian "Copyright Act" states:
>     42 (1)  Every person commits an offence who knowingly
>         (c)  distributes infringing copies of a work or other subject-matter in which copyright subsists, either for the purpose of trade or to such an extent as to affect prejudicially the owner of the copyright;

Section 42 , subsection (1) , paragraph (d)  of the Canadian "Copyright Act" states:
>     42 (1)  Every person commits an offence who knowingly
>         (d)  by way of trade exhibits in public an infringing copy of a work or other subject-matter in which copyright subsists;

Section 42 , subsection (1) , paragraph (e)  of the Canadian "Copyright Act" states:
>     42 (1)  Every person commits an offence who knowingly
>         (e)  possesses, for sale, rental, distribution for the purpose of trade or exhibition in public by way of trade, an infringing copy of a work or other subject-matter in which copyright subsists;

Section 42 , subsection (1) , paragraph (f)  of the Canadian "Copyright Act" states:
>     42 (1)  Every person commits an offence who knowingly
>         (f)  imports, for sale or rental, into Canada any infringing copy of a work or other subject-matter in which copyright subsists; or

Section 42 , subsection (1) , paragraph (g)  of the Canadian "Copyright Act" states:
>     42 (1)  Every person commits an offence who knowingly
>         (g)  exports or attempts to export, for sale or rental, an infringing copy of a work or other subject-matter in which copyright subsists.

Section 42 , subsection (2) , paragraph (a)  of the Canadian "Copyright Act" states:
>     42 (2)  Every person commits an offence who knowingly
>         (a)  makes or possesses any plate that is specifically designed or adapted for the purpose of making infringing copies of any work or other subject-matter in which copyright subsists; or

Section 42 , subsection (2) , paragraph (b)  of the Canadian "Copyright Act" states:
>     42 (2)  Every person commits an offence who knowingly
>         (b)  for private profit causes to be performed in public, without the consent of the owner of the copyright, any work or other subject-matter in which copyright subsists.

Section 42 , subsection (2.1) , paragraph (a)  of the Canadian "Copyright Act" states:
>     42 (2.1)  Every person who commits an offence under subsection (1) or (2) is liable
>         (a)  on conviction on indictment, to a fine of not more than $1,000,000 or to imprisonment for a term of not more than five years or to both; or

Section 42 , subsection (2.1) , paragraph (b)  of the Canadian "Copyright Act" states:
>     42 (2.1)  Every person who commits an offence under subsection (1) or (2) is liable
>         (b)  on summary conviction, to a fine of not more than $25,000 or to imprisonment for a term of not more than six months or to both.

Section 42 , subsection (3)  of the Canadian "Copyright Act" states:
>     42 (3)  The court before which any proceedings under this section are taken may, on conviction, order that all copies of the work or other subject-matter that appear to it to be infringing copies, or all plates in the possession of the offender predominantly used for making infringing copies, be destroyed or delivered up to the owner of the copyright or otherwise dealt with as the court may think fit.

Section 42 , subsection (3.01)  of the Canadian "Copyright Act" states:
>     42 (3.01)  Before making an order under subsection (3), the court shall require that notice be given to the owner of the copies or plates and to any other person who, in the court’s opinion, appears to have a right or interest in them, unless the court is of the opinion that the interests of justice do not require that the notice be given.

Section 42 , subsection (3.1) , paragraph (a)  of the Canadian "Copyright Act" states:
>     42 (3.1)  Every person, except a person who is acting on behalf of a library, archive or museum or an educational institution, is guilty of an offence who knowingly and for commercial purposes contravenes section 41.1 and is liable
>         (a)  on conviction on indictment, to a fine not exceeding $1,000,000 or to imprisonment for a term not exceeding five years or to both; or

Section 42 , subsection (3.1) , paragraph (b)  of the Canadian "Copyright Act" states:
>     42 (3.1)  Every person, except a person who is acting on behalf of a library, archive or museum or an educational institution, is guilty of an offence who knowingly and for commercial purposes contravenes section 41.1 and is liable
>         (b)  on summary conviction, to a fine not exceeding $25,000 or to imprisonment for a term not exceeding six months or to both.

Section 42 , subsection (3.2) , paragraph (a)  of the Canadian "Copyright Act" states:
>     42 (3.2)  Every person, except a person who is acting on behalf of a library, archive or museum or an educational institution, commits an offence who knowingly and for commercial purposes
>         (a)  removes or alters any rights management information in electronic form without the consent of the owner of the copyright in the work, the performer’s performance fixed in a sound recording or the sound recording, if the person knows that the removal or alteration will facilitate or conceal any infringement of the owner’s copyright or adversely affect the owner’s right to remuneration under section 19; or

Section 42 , subsection (3.2) , paragraph (b)  of the Canadian "Copyright Act" states:
>     42 (3.2)  Every person, except a person who is acting on behalf of a library, archive or museum or an educational institution, commits an offence who knowingly and for commercial purposes
>         (b)  does any of the acts referred to in paragraphs 41.22(3)(a) to (e) with respect to any material form of the work, the performer’s performance fixed in a sound recording or the sound recording without the consent of the owner of the copyright and knows that
>            (i)  the rights management information in electronic form has been removed or altered without the consent of the owner of the copyright, and
>            (ii)  the removal or alteration will facilitate or conceal any infringement of the owner’s copyright or adversely affect the owner’s right to remuneration under section 19.

Section 42 , subsection (3.3) , paragraph (a)  of the Canadian "Copyright Act" states:
>     42 (3.3)  Every person who commits an offence under subsection (3.2) is liable
>         (a)  on conviction on indictment to a fine of not more than $1,000,000 or to imprisonment for a term of not more than five years or to both; or

Section 42 , subsection (3.3) , paragraph (b)  of the Canadian "Copyright Act" states:
>     42 (3.3)  Every person who commits an offence under subsection (3.2) is liable
>         (b)  on summary conviction to a fine of not more than $25,000 or to imprisonment for a term of not more than six months or to both.

Section 42 , subsection (3.4)  of the Canadian "Copyright Act" states:
>     42 (3.4)  In subsection (3.2), rights management information has the same meaning as in subsection 41.22(4).

Section 42 , subsection (4)  of the Canadian "Copyright Act" states:
>     42 (4)  Proceedings by summary conviction in respect of an offence under this section may be instituted at any time within, but not later than, two years after the time when the offence was committed.

Section 42 , subsection (5)  of the Canadian "Copyright Act" states:
>     42 (5)  For the purposes of this section, a copy of a work or other subject-matter is not infringing if the copy was made with the consent of the owner of the copyright in the country where the copy was made.


Section 43  : Criminal Remedies / Infringement in case of dramatic, operatic or musical work
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

Section 43 , subsection (1)  of the Canadian "Copyright Act" states:
>     43 (1)  Any person who, without the written consent of the owner of the copyright or of the legal representative of the owner, knowingly performs or causes to be performed in public and for private profit the whole or any part, constituting an infringement, of any dramatic or operatic work or musical composition in which copyright subsists in Canada is guilty of an offence and liable on summary conviction to a fine not exceeding two hundred and fifty dollars and, in the case of a second or subsequent offence, either to that fine or to imprisonment for a term not exceeding two months or to both.

Section 43 , subsection (2)  of the Canadian "Copyright Act" states:
>     43 (2)  Any person who makes or causes to be made any change in or suppression of the title, or the name of the author, of any dramatic or operatic work or musical composition in which copyright subsists in Canada, or who makes or causes to be made any change in the work or composition itself without the written consent of the author or of his legal representative, in order that the work or composition may be performed in whole or in part in public for private profit, is guilty of an offence and liable on summary conviction to a fine not exceeding five hundred dollars and, in the case of a second or subsequent offence, either to that fine or to imprisonment for a term not exceeding four months or to both.


Section 43.1  : Limitation or Prescription Period / Limitation or prescription period for civil remedies
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

Section 43.1 , subsection (1) , paragraph (a)  of the Canadian "Copyright Act" states:
>     43.1 (1)  Subject to subsection (2), a court may award a remedy for any act or omission that has been done contrary to this Act only if
>         (a)  the proceedings for the act or omission giving rise to a remedy are commenced within three years after it occurred, in the case where the plaintiff knew, or could reasonably have been expected to know, of the act or omission at the time it occurred; or

Section 43.1 , subsection (1) , paragraph (b)  of the Canadian "Copyright Act" states:
>     43.1 (1)  Subject to subsection (2), a court may award a remedy for any act or omission that has been done contrary to this Act only if
>         (b)  the proceedings for the act or omission giving rise to a remedy are commenced within three years after the time when the plaintiff first knew of it, or could reasonably have been expected to know of it, in the case where the plaintiff did not know, and could not reasonably have been expected to know, of the act or omission at the time it occurred.

Section 43.1 , subsection (2)  of the Canadian "Copyright Act" states:
>     43.1 (2)  The court shall apply the limitation or prescription period set out in paragraph (1)(a) or (b) only in respect of a party who pleads a limitation period.


Section 44  : Interpretation / Definitions
------------------------------------------

Section 44  of the Canadian "Copyright Act" defines "court":
>     44  The following definitions apply in sections 44.02 to 44.4.
>         court: court means the Federal Court or the superior court of a province. (tribunal)


According to Section 44  of the Canadian "Copyright Act", "court" translate to French as "tribunal".

Section 44  of the Canadian "Copyright Act" defines "customs officer":
>     44  The following definitions apply in sections 44.02 to 44.4.
>         customs officer: customs officer has the meaning assigned by the definition officer in subsection 2(1) of the Customs Act. (agent des douanes)


According to Section 44  of the Canadian "Copyright Act", "customs officer" translate to French as "agent des douanes".

Section 44  of the Canadian "Copyright Act" defines "duties":
>     44  The following definitions apply in sections 44.02 to 44.4.
>         duties: duties has the same meaning as in subsection 2(1) of the Customs Act. (droits)


According to Section 44  of the Canadian "Copyright Act", "duties" translate to French as "droits".

Section 44  of the Canadian "Copyright Act" defines "Minister":
>     44  The following definitions apply in sections 44.02 to 44.4.
>         Minister: Minister means the Minister of Public Safety and Emergency Preparedness. (ministre)


According to Section 44  of the Canadian "Copyright Act", "Minister" translate to French as "ministre".

Section 44  of the Canadian "Copyright Act" defines "release":
>     44  The following definitions apply in sections 44.02 to 44.4.
>         release: release has the same meaning as in subsection 2(1) of the Customs Act. (dédouane­ment)


According to Section 44  of the Canadian "Copyright Act", "release" translate to French as "dédouane­ment".

Section 44  of the Canadian "Copyright Act" defines "working day":
>     44  The following definitions apply in sections 44.02 to 44.4.
>         working day: working day means a day other than a Saturday or a holiday. (jour ouvrable)


According to Section 44  of the Canadian "Copyright Act", "working day" translate to French as "jour ouvrable".


Section 44.01  : Prohibition / Prohibition on importation or exportation
------------------------------------------------------------------------

Section 44.01 , subsection (1) , paragraph (a)  of the Canadian "Copyright Act" states:
>     44.01 (1)  Copies of a work or other subject-matter in which copyright subsists shall not be imported or exported if
>         (a)  they were made without the consent of the owner of the copyright in the country where they were made; and

Section 44.01 , subsection (1) , paragraph (b)  of the Canadian "Copyright Act" states:
>     44.01 (1)  Copies of a work or other subject-matter in which copyright subsists shall not be imported or exported if
>         (b)  they infringe copyright or, if they were not made in Canada, they would infringe copyright had they been made in Canada by the person who made them.

Section 44.01 , subsection (2)  of the Canadian "Copyright Act" states:
>     44.01 (2)  Subsection (1) does not apply to copies that are imported or exported by an individual in their possession or baggage if the circumstances, including the number of copies, indicate that the copies are intended only for their personal use.


Section 44.02  : Request for Assistance / Request for assistance
----------------------------------------------------------------

Section 44.02 , subsection (1)  of the Canadian "Copyright Act" states:
>     44.02 (1)  The owner of copyright in a work or other subject-matter may file with the Minister, in the form and manner specified by the Minister, a request for assistance in pursuing remedies under this Act with respect to copies imported or exported in contravention of section 44.01.

Section 44.02 , subsection (2)  of the Canadian "Copyright Act" states:
>     44.02 (2)  The request for assistance shall include the copyright owner’s name and address in Canada and any other information that is required by the Minister, including information about the work or other subject-matter in question.

Section 44.02 , subsection (3)  of the Canadian "Copyright Act" states:
>     44.02 (3)  A request for assistance is valid for a period of two years beginning on the day on which it is accepted by the Minister. The Minister may, at the request of the copyright owner, extend the period for two years, and may do so more than once.

Section 44.02 , subsection (4)  of the Canadian "Copyright Act" states:
>     44.02 (4)  The Minister may, as a condition of accepting a request for assistance or of extending a request’s period of validity, require that the copyright owner furnish security, in an amount and form fixed by the Minister, for the payment of an amount for which the copyright owner becomes liable under section 44.07.

Section 44.02 , subsection (5) , paragraph (a)  of the Canadian "Copyright Act" states:
>     44.02 (5)  The copyright owner shall inform the Minister in writing, as soon as practicable, of any changes to
>         (a)  the subsistence of the copyright that is the subject of the request for assistance; or

Section 44.02 , subsection (5) , paragraph (b)  of the Canadian "Copyright Act" states:
>     44.02 (5)  The copyright owner shall inform the Minister in writing, as soon as practicable, of any changes to
>         (b)  the ownership of that copyright.


Section 44.03  : Measures Relating to Detained Copies / Provision of information by customs officer
---------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

Section 44.03  of the Canadian "Copyright Act" states:
>     A customs officer who is detaining copies of a work or other subject-matter under section 101 of the Customs Act may, in the officer’s discretion, to obtain information about whether the importation or exportation of the copies is prohibited under section 44.01, provide the owner of copyright in that work or subject-matter with a sample of the copies and with any information about the copies that the customs officer reasonably believes does not directly or indirectly identify any person.


Section 44.04  : Measures Relating to Detained Copies / Provision of information to pursue remedy
-------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

Section 44.04 , subsection (1) , paragraph (a)  of the Canadian "Copyright Act" states:
>     44.04 (1)  A customs officer who is detaining copies of a work or other subject-matter under section 101 of the Customs Act and who has reasonable grounds to suspect that the importation or exportation of the copies is prohibited under section 44.01 may, in the officer’s discretion, if the Minister has accepted a request for assistance with respect to the work or subject-matter filed by the owner of copyright in it, provide that owner with a sample of the copies and with information about the copies that could assist them in pursuing a remedy under this Act, such as
>         (a)  a description of the copies and of their characteristics;

Section 44.04 , subsection (1) , paragraph (b)  of the Canadian "Copyright Act" states:
>     44.04 (1)  A customs officer who is detaining copies of a work or other subject-matter under section 101 of the Customs Act and who has reasonable grounds to suspect that the importation or exportation of the copies is prohibited under section 44.01 may, in the officer’s discretion, if the Minister has accepted a request for assistance with respect to the work or subject-matter filed by the owner of copyright in it, provide that owner with a sample of the copies and with information about the copies that could assist them in pursuing a remedy under this Act, such as
>         (b)  the name and address of their owner, importer, exporter and consignee and of the person who made them and of any other person involved in their movement;

Section 44.04 , subsection (1) , paragraph (c)  of the Canadian "Copyright Act" states:
>     44.04 (1)  A customs officer who is detaining copies of a work or other subject-matter under section 101 of the Customs Act and who has reasonable grounds to suspect that the importation or exportation of the copies is prohibited under section 44.01 may, in the officer’s discretion, if the Minister has accepted a request for assistance with respect to the work or subject-matter filed by the owner of copyright in it, provide that owner with a sample of the copies and with information about the copies that could assist them in pursuing a remedy under this Act, such as
>         (c)  their quantity;

Section 44.04 , subsection (1) , paragraph (d)  of the Canadian "Copyright Act" states:
>     44.04 (1)  A customs officer who is detaining copies of a work or other subject-matter under section 101 of the Customs Act and who has reasonable grounds to suspect that the importation or exportation of the copies is prohibited under section 44.01 may, in the officer’s discretion, if the Minister has accepted a request for assistance with respect to the work or subject-matter filed by the owner of copyright in it, provide that owner with a sample of the copies and with information about the copies that could assist them in pursuing a remedy under this Act, such as
>         (d)  the countries in which they were made and through which they passed in transit; and

Section 44.04 , subsection (1) , paragraph (e)  of the Canadian "Copyright Act" states:
>     44.04 (1)  A customs officer who is detaining copies of a work or other subject-matter under section 101 of the Customs Act and who has reasonable grounds to suspect that the importation or exportation of the copies is prohibited under section 44.01 may, in the officer’s discretion, if the Minister has accepted a request for assistance with respect to the work or subject-matter filed by the owner of copyright in it, provide that owner with a sample of the copies and with information about the copies that could assist them in pursuing a remedy under this Act, such as
>         (e)  the day on which they were imported, if applicable.

Section 44.04 , subsection (2)  of the Canadian "Copyright Act" states:
>     44.04 (2)  Subject to subsection (3), the customs officer shall not detain, for the purpose of enforcing section 44.01, the copies for more than 10 working days  —  or, if the copies are perishable, for more than five days  —  after the day on which the customs officer first sends or makes available a sample or information to the copyright owner under subsection (1). At the request of the copyright owner made while the copies are detained for the purpose of enforcing section 44.01, the customs officer may, having regard to the circumstances, detain non-perishable copies for one additional period of not more than 10 working days.

Section 44.04 , subsection (3) , paragraph (a)  of the Canadian "Copyright Act" states:
>     44.04 (3)  If, before the copies are no longer detained for the purpose of enforcing section 44.01, the owner of copyright has provided the Minister, in the manner specified by the Minister, with a copy of a document filed with a court commencing proceedings to obtain a remedy under this Act with respect to the detained copies, the customs officer shall continue to detain them until the Minister is informed in writing that
>         (a)  the proceedings are finally disposed of, settled or abandoned;

Section 44.04 , subsection (3) , paragraph (b)  of the Canadian "Copyright Act" states:
>     44.04 (3)  If, before the copies are no longer detained for the purpose of enforcing section 44.01, the owner of copyright has provided the Minister, in the manner specified by the Minister, with a copy of a document filed with a court commencing proceedings to obtain a remedy under this Act with respect to the detained copies, the customs officer shall continue to detain them until the Minister is informed in writing that
>         (b)  a court directs that the copies are no longer to be detained for the purpose of the proceedings; or

Section 44.04 , subsection (3) , paragraph (c)  of the Canadian "Copyright Act" states:
>     44.04 (3)  If, before the copies are no longer detained for the purpose of enforcing section 44.01, the owner of copyright has provided the Minister, in the manner specified by the Minister, with a copy of a document filed with a court commencing proceedings to obtain a remedy under this Act with respect to the detained copies, the customs officer shall continue to detain them until the Minister is informed in writing that
>         (c)  the copyright owner consents to the copies no longer being so detained.

Section 44.04 , subsection (4)  of the Canadian "Copyright Act" states:
>     44.04 (4)  The occurrence of any of the events referred to in paragraphs (3)(a) to (c) does not preclude a customs officer from continuing to detain the copies under the Customs Act for a purpose other than the proceedings.


Section 44.05  : Measures Relating to Detained Copies / Restriction on information use  — section 44.03
-------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

Section 44.05 , subsection (1)  of the Canadian "Copyright Act" states:
>     44.05 (1)  A person who receives a sample or information that is provided under section 44.03 shall not use the information, or information that is derived from the sample, for any purpose other than to give information to the customs officer about whether the importation or exportation of the copies is prohibited under section 44.01.

Section 44.05 , subsection (2)  of the Canadian "Copyright Act" states:
>     44.05 (2)  A person who receives a sample or information that is provided under subsection 44.04(1) shall not use the information, or information that is derived from the sample, for any purpose other than to pursue remedies under this Act.

Section 44.05 , subsection (3)  of the Canadian "Copyright Act" states:
>     44.05 (3)  For greater certainty, subsection (2) does not prevent the confidential communication of information about the copies for the purpose of reaching an out-of-court settlement.


Section 44.06  : Measures Relating to Detained Copies / Inspection
------------------------------------------------------------------

Section 44.06  of the Canadian "Copyright Act" states:
>     After a sample or information has been provided under subsection 44.04(1), a customs officer may, in the officer’s discretion, give the owner, importer, exporter and consignee of the detained copies and the owner of copyright an opportunity to inspect the copies.


Section 44.07  : Measures Relating to Detained Copies / Liability for charges
-----------------------------------------------------------------------------

Section 44.07 , subsection (1) , paragraph (a)  of the Canadian "Copyright Act" states:
>     44.07 (1)  The owner of copyright who has received a sample or information under subsection 44.04(1) is liable to Her Majesty in right of Canada for the storage and handling charges for the detained copies  —  and, if applicable, for the charges for destroying them  —  for the period beginning on the day after the day on which a customs officer first sends or makes available a sample or information to that owner under that subsection and ending on the first day on which one of the following occurs:
>         (a)  the copies are no longer detained for the purpose of enforcing section 44.01 or, if subsection 44.04(3) applies, for the purpose of the proceedings referred to in that subsection;

Section 44.07 , subsection (1) , paragraph (b)  of the Canadian "Copyright Act" states:
>     44.07 (1)  The owner of copyright who has received a sample or information under subsection 44.04(1) is liable to Her Majesty in right of Canada for the storage and handling charges for the detained copies  —  and, if applicable, for the charges for destroying them  —  for the period beginning on the day after the day on which a customs officer first sends or makes available a sample or information to that owner under that subsection and ending on the first day on which one of the following occurs:
>         (b)  the Minister receives written notification in which the owner states that the importation or exportation of the copies does not, with respect to the owner’s copyright, contravene section 44.01;

Section 44.07 , subsection (1) , paragraph (c)  of the Canadian "Copyright Act" states:
>     44.07 (1)  The owner of copyright who has received a sample or information under subsection 44.04(1) is liable to Her Majesty in right of Canada for the storage and handling charges for the detained copies  —  and, if applicable, for the charges for destroying them  —  for the period beginning on the day after the day on which a customs officer first sends or makes available a sample or information to that owner under that subsection and ending on the first day on which one of the following occurs:
>         (c)  the Minister receives written notification in which the owner states that they will not, while the copies are detained for the purpose of enforcing section 44.01, commence proceedings to obtain a remedy under this Act with respect to them.

Section 44.07 , subsection (2)  of the Canadian "Copyright Act" states:
>     44.07 (2)  Despite paragraph (1)(a), if the copies are forfeited under subsection 39(1) of the Customs Act and the Minister did not, before the end of the detention of the copies for the purpose of enforcing section 44.01, receive a copy of a document filed with a court commencing proceedings to obtain a remedy under this Act with respect to the detained copies or the written notification referred to in paragraph (1)(b) or (c), the period ends on the day on which the copies are forfeited.

Section 44.07 , subsection (3)  of the Canadian "Copyright Act" states:
>     44.07 (3)  Despite paragraph (1)(c), if the copies are forfeited under subsection 39(1) of the Customs Act after the Minister has received the written notification referred to in that paragraph, the period ends on the day on which the copies are forfeited.

Section 44.07 , subsection (4) , paragraph (a)  of the Canadian "Copyright Act" states:
>     44.07 (4)  The owner and the importer or exporter of copies that are forfeited in the circumstances set out in subsection (2) or (3) are jointly and severally, or solidarily, liable to the owner of copyright for all the charges under subsection (1) paid by the copyright owner with respect to the period
>         (a)  in the circumstances referred to in subsection (2), beginning on the day on which the copies are no longer detained for the purpose of enforcing section 44.01 and ending on the day on which the copies are forfeited; and

Section 44.07 , subsection (4) , paragraph (b)  of the Canadian "Copyright Act" states:
>     44.07 (4)  The owner and the importer or exporter of copies that are forfeited in the circumstances set out in subsection (2) or (3) are jointly and severally, or solidarily, liable to the owner of copyright for all the charges under subsection (1) paid by the copyright owner with respect to the period
>         (b)  in the circumstances referred to in subsection (3), beginning on the day on which the Minister receives the written notification referred to in paragraph (1)(c) and ending on the day on which the copies are forfeited.

Section 44.07 , subsection (5) , paragraph (a)  of the Canadian "Copyright Act" states:
>     44.07 (5)  Subsections (1) to (3) do not apply if
>         (a)  the detention of the copies for the purpose of enforcing section 44.01 ends before the expiry of 10 working days  —  or, if the copies are perishable, before the expiry of five days  —  after the day on which the customs officer first sends or makes available a sample or information to the copyright owner under subsection 44.04(1); and

Section 44.07 , subsection (5) , paragraph (b)  of the Canadian "Copyright Act" states:
>     44.07 (5)  Subsections (1) to (3) do not apply if
>         (b)  the Minister has not, by the end of the detention, received a copy of a document filed with a court commencing proceedings to obtain a remedy under this Act with respect to the detained copies or the written notification referred to in paragraph (1)(b) or (c).


Section 44.08  : No Liability / No liability
--------------------------------------------

Section 44.08 , paragraph (a)  of the Canadian "Copyright Act" states:
>     44.08  Neither Her Majesty nor a customs officer is liable for any loss or damage suffered in relation to the enforcement or application of sections 44.01 to 44.04 and 44.06 because of
>         (a)  the detention of copies of a work or other subject-matter, except if the detention contravenes subsection 44.04(2);

Section 44.08 , paragraph (b)  of the Canadian "Copyright Act" states:
>     44.08  Neither Her Majesty nor a customs officer is liable for any loss or damage suffered in relation to the enforcement or application of sections 44.01 to 44.04 and 44.06 because of
>         (b)  the failure to detain copies; or

Section 44.08 , paragraph (c)  of the Canadian "Copyright Act" states:
>     44.08  Neither Her Majesty nor a customs officer is liable for any loss or damage suffered in relation to the enforcement or application of sections 44.01 to 44.04 and 44.06 because of
>         (c)  the release or cessation of detention of any copies, except if the release or cessation contravenes subsection 44.04(3).


Section 44.09  : Powers of Court Relating to Detained Copies / Application to court
-----------------------------------------------------------------------------------

Section 44.09 , subsection (1) , paragraph (a)  of the Canadian "Copyright Act" states:
>     44.09 (1)  In the course of proceedings referred to in subsection 44.04(3), the court may, on the application of the Minister or a party to the proceedings,
>         (a)  impose conditions on the storage or detention of the copies that are the subject of the proceedings; or

Section 44.09 , subsection (1) , paragraph (b)  of the Canadian "Copyright Act" states:
>     44.09 (1)  In the course of proceedings referred to in subsection 44.04(3), the court may, on the application of the Minister or a party to the proceedings,
>         (b)  direct that the copies are no longer to be detained for the purpose of the proceedings, on any conditions that the court may impose, if their owner, importer, exporter or consignee furnishes security in an amount fixed by the court.

Section 44.09 , subsection (2)  of the Canadian "Copyright Act" states:
>     44.09 (2)  If a party applies to have the detained copies stored in a place other than a bonded warehouse or a sufferance warehouse, as those terms are defined in subsection 2(1) of the Customs Act, the Minister must consent to the storage of the copies in that place before a condition to that effect is imposed under subsection (1).

Section 44.09 , subsection (3)  of the Canadian "Copyright Act" states:
>     44.09 (3)  The court may impose a condition described in subsection (2) despite section 31 of the Customs Act.

Section 44.09 , subsection (4)  of the Canadian "Copyright Act" states:
>     44.09 (4)  A direction under paragraph (1)(b) that the copies are no longer to be detained for the purpose of the proceedings does not preclude a customs officer from continuing to detain the copies under the Customs Act for another purpose.

Section 44.09 , subsection (5) , paragraph (a)  of the Canadian "Copyright Act" states:
>     44.09 (5)  In the course of proceedings referred to in subsection 44.04(3), the court may, on the application of the Minister or a party to the proceedings, require the owner of copyright to furnish security, in an amount fixed by the court,
>         (a)  to cover duties, storage and handling charges, and any other amount that may become chargeable against the copies; and

Section 44.09 , subsection (5) , paragraph (b)  of the Canadian "Copyright Act" states:
>     44.09 (5)  In the course of proceedings referred to in subsection 44.04(3), the court may, on the application of the Minister or a party to the proceedings, require the owner of copyright to furnish security, in an amount fixed by the court,
>         (b)  to answer any damages that may, because of the detention of the copies, be sustained by the owner, importer, exporter or consignee of the copies.


Section 44.1  : Powers of Court Relating to Detained Copies / Damages against copyright owner
---------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

Section 44.1 , subsection (1)  of the Canadian "Copyright Act" states:
>     44.1 (1)  The court may award damages against the owner of copyright who commenced proceedings referred to in subsection 44.04(3) to the owner, importer, exporter or consignee of the copies who is a party to the proceedings for losses, costs or prejudice suffered as a result of the detention of the copies if the proceedings are dismissed or discontinued.

Section 44.1 , subsection (2)  of the Canadian "Copyright Act" states:
>     44.1 (2)  Any damages under subsection 34(1) awarded to the owner of copyright in proceedings referred to in subsection 44.04(3) are to include the charges incurred by the copyright owner as a result of storing, handling or, if applicable, destroying the detained copies.


Section 44.11  : Prohibition Resulting from Notice / Importation of certain copyright works prohibited
------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

Section 44.11  of the Canadian "Copyright Act" states:
>     Copies made outside Canada of any work in which copyright subsists that if made in Canada would infringe copyright and as to which the owner of the copyright gives notice in writing to the Canada Border Services Agency that the owner desires that the copies not be imported into Canada, shall not be so imported and are deemed to be included in tariff item No. 9897.00.00 in the List of Tariff Provisions set out in the schedule to the Customs Tariff, with section 136 of that Act applying accordingly.


Section 44.12  : Court-ordered Detention / Power of court
---------------------------------------------------------

Section 44.12 , subsection (1) , paragraph (a)  of the Canadian "Copyright Act" states:
>     44.12 (1)  A court may make an order described in subsection (3) if the court is satisfied that
>         (a)  copies of the work are about to be imported into Canada, or have been imported into Canada but have not been released;

Section 44.12 , subsection (1) , paragraph (b)  of the Canadian "Copyright Act" states:
>     44.12 (1)  A court may make an order described in subsection (3) if the court is satisfied that
>         (b)  the copies were either
>            (i)  made without the consent of the person who is owner of the copyright in the country where they were made, or
>            (ii)  made elsewhere than in a country to which this Act extends; and

Section 44.12 , subsection (1) , paragraph (c)  of the Canadian "Copyright Act" states:
>     44.12 (1)  A court may make an order described in subsection (3) if the court is satisfied that
>         (c)  the copies would infringe copyright if they were made in Canada by the importer and the importer knows or should have known this.

Section 44.12 , subsection (2)  of the Canadian "Copyright Act" states:
>     44.12 (2)  A court may make an order described in subsection (3) on application by the owner of the copyright in a work in Canada.

Section 44.12 , subsection (3) , paragraph (a)  of the Canadian "Copyright Act" states:
>     44.12 (3)  In an order made under subsection (1), the court may
>         (a)  direct the Minister
>            (i)  to take reasonable measures, on the basis of information reasonably required by the Minister and provided by the applicant, to detain the copies of the work, and
>            (ii)  to notify the applicant and the importer, immediately after detaining the copies of the work, of the detention and the reasons for the detention; and

Section 44.12 , subsection (3) , paragraph (b)  of the Canadian "Copyright Act" states:
>     44.12 (3)  In an order made under subsection (1), the court may
>         (b)  provide for any other matters that the court considers appropriate.

Section 44.12 , subsection (4)  of the Canadian "Copyright Act" states:
>     44.12 (4)  An application for an order under subsection (1) may be made in an action or otherwise, and either on notice or ex parte, except that it must always be made on notice to the Minister.

Section 44.12 , subsection (5) , paragraph (a)  of the Canadian "Copyright Act" states:
>     44.12 (5)  Before making an order under subsection (1), the court may require the applicant to furnish security, in an amount fixed by the court,
>         (a)  to cover duties, storage and handling charges and any other amount that may become chargeable against the copies of the work; and

Section 44.12 , subsection (5) , paragraph (b)  of the Canadian "Copyright Act" states:
>     44.12 (5)  Before making an order under subsection (1), the court may require the applicant to furnish security, in an amount fixed by the court,
>         (b)  to answer any damages that may by reason of the order be incurred by the owner, importer or consignee of the work.

Section 44.12 , subsection (6)  of the Canadian "Copyright Act" states:
>     44.12 (6)  The Minister may apply to the court for directions in implementing an order made under subsection (1).

Section 44.12 , subsection (7)  of the Canadian "Copyright Act" states:
>     44.12 (7)  The Minister may give the applicant or the importer an opportunity to inspect the detained copies of the work for the purpose of substantiating or refuting, as the case may be, the applicant’s claim.

Section 44.12 , subsection (8)  of the Canadian "Copyright Act" states:
>     44.12 (8)  Unless an order made under subsection (1) provides otherwise, the Minister shall, subject to the Customs Act and to any other Act of Parliament that prohibits, controls or regulates the importation or exportation of goods, release the copies of the work without further notice to the applicant if, within 10 working days after the applicant has been notified under subparagraph (3)(a)(ii), the applicant has not notified the Minister that they have commenced a proceeding for a final determination by the court of the issues referred to in paragraphs (1)(b) and (c).

Section 44.12 , subsection (9)  of the Canadian "Copyright Act" states:
>     44.12 (9)  If, in a proceeding commenced under this section, the court is satisfied that the circumstances referred to in paragraphs (1)(b) and (c) existed, the court may make any order that it considers appropriate in the circumstances, including an order that the copies of the work be destroyed, or that they be delivered up to the plaintiff as the plaintiff’s property absolutely.

Section 44.12 , subsection (10)  of the Canadian "Copyright Act" states:
>     44.12 (10)  For greater certainty, nothing in this section affects any remedy available under any other provision of this Act or any other Act of Parliament.


Section 44.2  : Court-ordered Detention / Importation of books
--------------------------------------------------------------

Section 44.2 , subsection (1) , paragraph (a)  of the Canadian "Copyright Act" states:
>     44.2 (1)  A court may, subject to this section, make an order described in subsection 44.12(3) in relation to a book where the court is satisfied that
>         (a)  copies of the book are about to be imported into Canada, or have been imported into Canada but have not yet been released;

Section 44.2 , subsection (1) , paragraph (b)  of the Canadian "Copyright Act" states:
>     44.2 (1)  A court may, subject to this section, make an order described in subsection 44.12(3) in relation to a book where the court is satisfied that
>         (b)  copies of the book were made with the consent of the owner of the copyright in the book in the country where the copies were made, but were imported without the consent of the owner in Canada of the copyright in the book; and

Section 44.2 , subsection (1) , paragraph (c)  of the Canadian "Copyright Act" states:
>     44.2 (1)  A court may, subject to this section, make an order described in subsection 44.12(3) in relation to a book where the court is satisfied that
>         (c)  the copies would infringe copyright if they were made in Canada by the importer and the importer knows or should have known this.

Section 44.2 , subsection (2) , paragraph (a)  of the Canadian "Copyright Act" states:
>     44.2 (2)  A court may make an order described in subsection 44.12(3) in relation to a book on application by
>         (a)  the owner of the copyright in the book in Canada;

Section 44.2 , subsection (2) , paragraph (b)  of the Canadian "Copyright Act" states:
>     44.2 (2)  A court may make an order described in subsection 44.12(3) in relation to a book on application by
>         (b)  the exclusive licensee of the copyright in the book in Canada; or

Section 44.2 , subsection (2) , paragraph (c)  of the Canadian "Copyright Act" states:
>     44.2 (2)  A court may make an order described in subsection 44.12(3) in relation to a book on application by
>         (c)  the exclusive distributor of the book.

Section 44.2 , subsection (3)  of the Canadian "Copyright Act" states:
>     44.2 (3)  Subsections (1) and (2) only apply where there is an exclusive distributor of the book and the acts described in those subsections take place in the part of Canada or in respect of the particular sector of the market for which the person is the exclusive distributor.

Section 44.2 , subsection (4)  of the Canadian "Copyright Act" states:
>     44.2 (4)  Subsections 44.12(3) to (10) apply, with such modifications as the circumstances require, in respect of an order made under subsection (1).


Section 44.3  : Court-ordered Detention / Limitation
----------------------------------------------------

Section 44.3  of the Canadian "Copyright Act" states:
>     No exclusive licensee of the copyright in a book in Canada, and no exclusive distributor of a book, may obtain an order under section 44.2 against another exclusive licensee of the copyright in that book in Canada or against another exclusive distributor of that book.


Section 44.4  : Court-ordered Detention / Importation of other subject-matter
-----------------------------------------------------------------------------

Section 44.4 , paragraph (a)  of the Canadian "Copyright Act" states:
>     44.4  Section 44.12 applies, with such modifications as the circumstances require, in respect of a sound recording, performer’s performance or communication signal, where a fixation or a reproduction of a fixation of it
>         (a)  is about to be imported into Canada, or has been imported into Canada but has not yet been released;

Section 44.4 , paragraph (b) , subparagraph (i)  of the Canadian "Copyright Act" states:
>     44.4  Section 44.12 applies, with such modifications as the circumstances require, in respect of a sound recording, performer’s performance or communication signal, where a fixation or a reproduction of a fixation of it
>         (b)  either
>             (i)  was made without the consent of the person who then owned the copyright in the sound recording, performer’s performance or communication signal, as the case may be, in the country where the fixation or reproduction was made, or

Section 44.4 , paragraph (b) , subparagraph (ii)  of the Canadian "Copyright Act" states:
>     44.4  Section 44.12 applies, with such modifications as the circumstances require, in respect of a sound recording, performer’s performance or communication signal, where a fixation or a reproduction of a fixation of it
>         (b)  either
>             (ii)  was made elsewhere than in a country to which Part II extends; and

Section 44.4 , paragraph (c)  of the Canadian "Copyright Act" states:
>     44.4  Section 44.12 applies, with such modifications as the circumstances require, in respect of a sound recording, performer’s performance or communication signal, where a fixation or a reproduction of a fixation of it
>         (c)  would infringe the right of the owner of copyright in the sound recording, performer’s performance or communication signal if it was made in Canada by the importer and the importer knows or should have known this.


Section 45  : Court-ordered Detention / Exceptions
--------------------------------------------------

Section 45 , subsection (1) , paragraph (a)  of the Canadian "Copyright Act" states:
>     45 (1)  Notwithstanding anything in this Act, it is lawful for a person
>         (a)  to import for their own use not more than two copies of a work or other subject-matter made with the consent of the owner of the copyright in the country where it was made;

Section 45 , subsection (1) , paragraph (b)  of the Canadian "Copyright Act" states:
>     45 (1)  Notwithstanding anything in this Act, it is lawful for a person
>         (b)  to import for use by a department of the Government of Canada or a province copies of a work or other subject-matter made with the consent of the owner of the copyright in the country where it was made;

Section 45 , subsection (1) , paragraph (c)  of the Canadian "Copyright Act" states:
>     45 (1)  Notwithstanding anything in this Act, it is lawful for a person
>         (c)  at any time before copies of a work or other subject-matter are made in Canada, to import any copies, except copies of a book, made with the consent of the owner of the copyright in the country where the copies were made, that are required for the use of a library, archive, museum or educational institution;

Section 45 , subsection (1) , paragraph (d)  of the Canadian "Copyright Act" states:
>     45 (1)  Notwithstanding anything in this Act, it is lawful for a person
>         (d)  to import, for the use of a library, archive, museum or educational institution, not more than one copy of a book that is made with the consent of the owner of the copyright in the country where the book was made; and

Section 45 , subsection (1) , paragraph (e)  of the Canadian "Copyright Act" states:
>     45 (1)  Notwithstanding anything in this Act, it is lawful for a person
>         (e)  to import copies, made with the consent of the owner of the copyright in the country where they were made, of any used books, except textbooks of a scientific, technical or scholarly nature for use within an educational institution in a course of instruction.

Section 45 , subsection (2)  of the Canadian "Copyright Act" states:
>     45 (2)  An officer of customs may, in the officer’s discretion, require a person seeking to import a copy of a work or other subject-matter under this section to produce satisfactory evidence of the facts necessary to establish the person’s right to import the copy.


Section 46  : Copyright Office / Copyright Office
-------------------------------------------------

Section 46  of the Canadian "Copyright Act" states:
>     The Copyright Office shall be attached to the Patent Office.


Section 47  : Copyright Office / Powers of Commissioner and Registrar
---------------------------------------------------------------------

Section 47  of the Canadian "Copyright Act" states:
>     The Commissioner of Patents shall exercise the powers conferred and perform the duties imposed on him by this Act under the direction of the Minister, and, in the absence of the Commissioner of Patents or if the Commissioner is unable to act, the Registrar of Copyrights or other officer temporarily appointed by the Minister may, as Acting Commissioner, exercise those powers and perform those duties under the direction of the Minister.


Section 48  : Copyright Office / Registrar
------------------------------------------

Section 48  of the Canadian "Copyright Act" states:
>     There shall be a Registrar of Copyrights.


Section 49  : Copyright Office / Register of Copyrights, certificates and certified copies
------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

Section 49  of the Canadian "Copyright Act" states:
>     The Commissioner of Patents, the Registrar of Copyrights or an officer, clerk or employee of the Copyright Office may sign certificates and certified copies of the Register of Copyrights.


Section 50  : Copyright Office / Other duties of Registrar
----------------------------------------------------------

Section 50  of the Canadian "Copyright Act" states:
>     The Registrar of Copyrights shall perform such other duties in connection with the administration of this Act as may be assigned to him by the Commissioner of Patents.


Section 51  : Copyright Office / 
---------------------------------

Section 51  of the Canadian "Copyright Act", was repealed: [Repealed, 1992, c. 1, s. 48]


Section 52  : Copyright Office / Control of business and officials
------------------------------------------------------------------

Section 52  of the Canadian "Copyright Act" states:
>     The Commissioner of Patents shall, subject to the Minister, oversee and direct the officers, clerks and employees of the Copyright Office, have general control of the business thereof and perform such other duties as are assigned to him by the Governor in Council.


Section 53  : Copyright Office / Register to be evidence
--------------------------------------------------------

Section 53 , subsection (1)  of the Canadian "Copyright Act" states:
>     53 (1)  The Register of Copyrights is evidence of the particulars entered in it, and a copy of an entry in the Register is evidence of the particulars of the entry if it is certified by the Commissioner of Patents, the Registrar of Copyrights or an officer, clerk or employee of the Copyright Office as a true copy.

Section 53 , subsection (2)  of the Canadian "Copyright Act" states:
>     53 (2)  A certificate of registration of copyright is evidence that the copyright subsists and that the person registered is the owner of the copyright.

Section 53 , subsection (2.1)  of the Canadian "Copyright Act" states:
>     53 (2.1)  A certificate of registration of an assignment of copyright is evidence that the right recorded on the certificate has been assigned and that the assignee registered is the owner of that right.

Section 53 , subsection (2.2)  of the Canadian "Copyright Act" states:
>     53 (2.2)  A certificate of registration of a licence granting an interest in a copyright is evidence that the interest recorded on the certificate has been granted and that the licensee registered is the holder of that interest.

Section 53 , subsection (3)  of the Canadian "Copyright Act" states:
>     53 (3)  A certified copy or certificate appearing to have been issued under this section is admissible in all courts without proof of the signature or official character of the person appearing to have signed it.


Section 54  : Registration / Register of Copyrights
---------------------------------------------------

Section 54 , subsection (1) , paragraph (a)  of the Canadian "Copyright Act" states:
>     54 (1)  The Minister shall cause to be kept at the Copyright Office a register to be called the Register of Copyrights in which may be entered
>         (a)  the names or titles of works and of other subject-matter in which copyright subsists;

Section 54 , subsection (1) , paragraph (b)  of the Canadian "Copyright Act" states:
>     54 (1)  The Minister shall cause to be kept at the Copyright Office a register to be called the Register of Copyrights in which may be entered
>         (b)  the names and addresses of authors, performers, makers of sound recordings, broadcasters, owners of copyright, assignees of copyright, and persons to whom an interest in copyright has been granted by licence; and

Section 54 , subsection (1) , paragraph (c)  of the Canadian "Copyright Act" states:
>     54 (1)  The Minister shall cause to be kept at the Copyright Office a register to be called the Register of Copyrights in which may be entered
>         (c)  such other particulars as may be prescribed by regulation.

Section 54 , subsection (2)  of the Canadian "Copyright Act" states:
>     54 (2)  [Repealed, 1997, c. 24, s. 31]

Section 54 , subsection (3)  of the Canadian "Copyright Act" states:
>     54 (3)  In the case of an encyclopaedia, newspaper, review, magazine or other periodical work, or work published in a series of books or parts, it is not necessary to make a separate entry for each number or part, but a single entry for the whole work is sufficient.

Section 54 , subsection (4)  of the Canadian "Copyright Act" states:
>     54 (4)  There shall also be kept at the Copyright Office such indices of the Register established under this section as may be prescribed by regulation.

Section 54 , subsection (5)  of the Canadian "Copyright Act" states:
>     54 (5)  The Register and indices established under this section shall at all reasonable times be open to inspection, and any person is entitled to make copies of or take extracts from the Register.

Section 54 , subsection (6)  of the Canadian "Copyright Act" states:
>     54 (6)  Any registration made under the Copyright Act, chapter 70 of the Revised Statutes of Canada, 1906, has the same force and effect as if made under this Act.

Section 54 , subsection (7)  of the Canadian "Copyright Act" states:
>     54 (7)  Any work in which copyright, operative in Canada, subsisted immediately before January 1, 1924 is registrable under this Act.


Section 55  : Registration / Copyright in works
-----------------------------------------------

Section 55 , subsection (1)  of the Canadian "Copyright Act" states:
>     55 (1)  Application for the registration of a copyright in a work may be made by or on behalf of the author of the work, the owner of the copyright in the work, an assignee of the copyright, or a person to whom an interest in the copyright has been granted by licence.

Section 55 , subsection (2) , paragraph (a)  of the Canadian "Copyright Act" states:
>     55 (2)  An application under subsection (1) must be filed with the Copyright Office, be accompanied by the fee prescribed by or determined under the regulations, and contain the following information:
>         (a)  the name and address of the owner of the copyright in the work;

Section 55 , subsection (2) , paragraph (b)  of the Canadian "Copyright Act" states:
>     55 (2)  An application under subsection (1) must be filed with the Copyright Office, be accompanied by the fee prescribed by or determined under the regulations, and contain the following information:
>         (b)  a declaration that the applicant is the author of the work, the owner of the copyright in the work, an assignee of the copyright, or a person to whom an interest in the copyright has been granted by licence;

Section 55 , subsection (2) , paragraph (c)  of the Canadian "Copyright Act" states:
>     55 (2)  An application under subsection (1) must be filed with the Copyright Office, be accompanied by the fee prescribed by or determined under the regulations, and contain the following information:
>         (c)  the category of the work;

Section 55 , subsection (2) , paragraph (d)  of the Canadian "Copyright Act" states:
>     55 (2)  An application under subsection (1) must be filed with the Copyright Office, be accompanied by the fee prescribed by or determined under the regulations, and contain the following information:
>         (d)  the title of the work;

Section 55 , subsection (2) , paragraph (e)  of the Canadian "Copyright Act" states:
>     55 (2)  An application under subsection (1) must be filed with the Copyright Office, be accompanied by the fee prescribed by or determined under the regulations, and contain the following information:
>         (e)  the name of the author and, if the author is dead, the date of the author’s death, if known;

Section 55 , subsection (2) , paragraph (f)  of the Canadian "Copyright Act" states:
>     55 (2)  An application under subsection (1) must be filed with the Copyright Office, be accompanied by the fee prescribed by or determined under the regulations, and contain the following information:
>         (f)  in the case of a published work, the date and place of the first publication; and

Section 55 , subsection (2) , paragraph (g)  of the Canadian "Copyright Act" states:
>     55 (2)  An application under subsection (1) must be filed with the Copyright Office, be accompanied by the fee prescribed by or determined under the regulations, and contain the following information:
>         (g)  any additional information prescribed by regulation.


Section 56  : Registration / Copyright in subject-matter other than works
-------------------------------------------------------------------------

Section 56 , subsection (1)  of the Canadian "Copyright Act" states:
>     56 (1)  Application for the registration of a copyright in subject-matter other than a work may be made by or on behalf of the owner of the copyright in the subject-matter, an assignee of the copyright, or a person to whom an interest in the copyright has been granted by licence.

Section 56 , subsection (2) , paragraph (a)  of the Canadian "Copyright Act" states:
>     56 (2)  An application under subsection (1) must be filed with the Copyright Office, be accompanied by the fee prescribed by or determined under the regulations, and contain the following information:
>         (a)  the name and address of the owner of the copyright in the subject-matter;

Section 56 , subsection (2) , paragraph (b)  of the Canadian "Copyright Act" states:
>     56 (2)  An application under subsection (1) must be filed with the Copyright Office, be accompanied by the fee prescribed by or determined under the regulations, and contain the following information:
>         (b)  a declaration that the applicant is the owner of the copyright in the subject-matter, an assignee of the copyright, or a person to whom an interest in the copyright has been granted by licence;

Section 56 , subsection (2) , paragraph (c)  of the Canadian "Copyright Act" states:
>     56 (2)  An application under subsection (1) must be filed with the Copyright Office, be accompanied by the fee prescribed by or determined under the regulations, and contain the following information:
>         (c)  whether the subject-matter is a performer’s performance, a sound recording or a communication signal;

Section 56 , subsection (2) , paragraph (d)  of the Canadian "Copyright Act" states:
>     56 (2)  An application under subsection (1) must be filed with the Copyright Office, be accompanied by the fee prescribed by or determined under the regulations, and contain the following information:
>         (d)  the title, if any, of the subject-matter;

Section 56 , subsection (2) , paragraph (e)  of the Canadian "Copyright Act" states:
>     56 (2)  An application under subsection (1) must be filed with the Copyright Office, be accompanied by the fee prescribed by or determined under the regulations, and contain the following information:
>         (e)  the date of
>            (i)  in the case of a performer’s performance, its first fixation in a sound recording or, if it is not fixed in a sound recording, its first performance,
>            (ii)  in the case of a sound recording, the first fixation, or
>            (iii)  in the case of a communication signal, its broadcast; and

Section 56 , subsection (2) , paragraph (f)  of the Canadian "Copyright Act" states:
>     56 (2)  An application under subsection (1) must be filed with the Copyright Office, be accompanied by the fee prescribed by or determined under the regulations, and contain the following information:
>         (f)  any additional information prescribed by regulation.


Section 56.1  : Registration / Recovery of damages
--------------------------------------------------

Section 56.1  of the Canadian "Copyright Act" states:
>     Where a person purports to have the authority to apply for the registration of a copyright under section 55 or 56 on behalf of another person, any damage caused by a fraudulent or erroneous assumption of such authority is recoverable in any court of competent jurisdiction.


Section 57  : Registration / Registration of assignment or licence
------------------------------------------------------------------

Section 57 , subsection (1) , paragraph (a)  of the Canadian "Copyright Act" states:
>     57 (1)  The Registrar of Copyrights shall register an assignment of copyright, or a licence granting an interest in a copyright, on being furnished with
>         (a)  the original instrument or a certified copy of it, or other evidence satisfactory to the Registrar of the assignment or licence; and

Section 57 , subsection (1) , paragraph (b)  of the Canadian "Copyright Act" states:
>     57 (1)  The Registrar of Copyrights shall register an assignment of copyright, or a licence granting an interest in a copyright, on being furnished with
>         (b)  the fee prescribed by or determined under the regulations.

Section 57 , subsection (2)  of the Canadian "Copyright Act" states:
>     57 (2)  [Repealed, 1992, c. 1, s. 51]

Section 57 , subsection (3)  of the Canadian "Copyright Act" states:
>     57 (3)  Any assignment of copyright, or any licence granting an interest in a copyright, shall be adjudged void against any subsequent assignee or licensee for valuable consideration without actual notice, unless the prior assignment or licence is registered in the manner prescribed by this Act before the registering of the instrument under which the subsequent assignee or licensee claims.

Section 57 , subsection (4) , paragraph (a)  of the Canadian "Copyright Act" states:
>     57 (4)  The Federal Court may, on application of the Registrar of Copyrights or of any interested person, order the rectification of the Register of Copyrights by
>         (a)  the making of any entry wrongly omitted to be made in the Register,

Section 57 , subsection (4) , paragraph (b)  of the Canadian "Copyright Act" states:
>     57 (4)  The Federal Court may, on application of the Registrar of Copyrights or of any interested person, order the rectification of the Register of Copyrights by
>         (b)  the expunging of any entry wrongly made in or remaining on the Register, or

Section 57 , subsection (4) , paragraph (c)  of the Canadian "Copyright Act" states:
>     57 (4)  The Federal Court may, on application of the Registrar of Copyrights or of any interested person, order the rectification of the Register of Copyrights by
>         (c)  the correction of any error or defect in the Register,


Section 58  : Registration / Execution of instruments
-----------------------------------------------------

Section 58 , subsection (1)  of the Canadian "Copyright Act" states:
>     58 (1)  Any assignment of a copyright, or any licence granting an interest in a copyright, may be executed, subscribed or acknowledged at any place in a treaty country, a Rome Convention country or a WPPT country by the assignor, licensor or secured or hypothecary debtor, before any notary public, commissioner or other official, or the judge of any court, who is authorized by law to administer oaths or certify documents in that place and who also subscribes their signature and affixes to, or impresses on, the assignment or licence their official seal or the seal of the court of which they are a judge.

Section 58 , subsection (2)  of the Canadian "Copyright Act" states:
>     58 (2)  Any assignment of copyright, or any licence granting an interest in a copyright, may be executed, subscribed or acknowledged by the assignor, licensor or mortgagor, in any other foreign country before any notary public, commissioner or other official or the judge of any court of the foreign country, who is authorized to administer oaths or perform notarial acts in that foreign country and whose authority shall be proved by the certificate of a diplomatic or consular officer of Canada performing their functions in that foreign country.

Section 58 , subsection (3)  of the Canadian "Copyright Act" states:
>     58 (3)  The official seal or seal of the court or the certificate of a diplomatic or consular officer is evidence of the execution of the instrument, and the instrument with the seal or certificate affixed or attached thereto is admissible as evidence in any action or proceeding brought under this Act without further proof.

Section 58 , subsection (4)  of the Canadian "Copyright Act" states:
>     58 (4)  The provisions of subsections (1) and (2) shall be deemed to be permissive only, and the execution of any assignment of copyright, or any licence granting an interest in a copyright, may in any case be proved in accordance with the applicable rules of evidence.


Section 59  : Fees / Fees regulations
-------------------------------------

Section 59 , paragraph (a)  of the Canadian "Copyright Act" states:
>     59  The Governor in Council may make regulations
>         (a)  prescribing fees, or the manner of determining fees, to be paid for anything required or authorized to be done in the administration of this Act; and

Section 59 , paragraph (b)  of the Canadian "Copyright Act" states:
>     59  The Governor in Council may make regulations
>         (b)  prescribing the time and manner in which the fees must be paid.


Section 60  : Substituted Right / Subsistence of substituted right
------------------------------------------------------------------

Section 60 , subsection (1)  of the Canadian "Copyright Act" states:
>     60 (1)  Where any person is immediately before January 1, 1924 entitled to any right in any work that is set out in column I of Schedule I, or to any interest in such a right, he is, as from that date, entitled to the substituted right set out in column II of that Schedule, or to the same interest in the substituted right, and to no other right or interest, and the substituted right shall subsist for the term for which it would have subsisted if this Act had been in force at the date when the work was made, and the work had been one entitled to copyright thereunder.

Section 60 , subsection (2) , paragraph (a)  of the Canadian "Copyright Act" states:
