>     60 (2)  Where the author of any work in which any right that is set out in column I of Schedule I subsists on January 1, 1924 has, before that date, assigned the right or granted any interest therein for the whole term of the right, then at the date when, but for the passing of this Act, the right would have expired, the substituted right conferred by this section shall, in the absence of express agreement, pass to the author of the work, and any interest therein created before January 1, 1924 and then subsisting shall determine, but the person who immediately before the date at which the right would have expired was the owner of the right or interest is entitled at his option either
>         (a)  on giving such notice as is hereinafter mentioned, to an assignment of the right or the grant of a similar interest therein for the remainder of the term of the right for such consideration as, failing agreement, may be determined by arbitration, or

Section 60 , subsection (2) , paragraph (b)  of the Canadian "Copyright Act" states:
>     60 (2)  Where the author of any work in which any right that is set out in column I of Schedule I subsists on January 1, 1924 has, before that date, assigned the right or granted any interest therein for the whole term of the right, then at the date when, but for the passing of this Act, the right would have expired, the substituted right conferred by this section shall, in the absence of express agreement, pass to the author of the work, and any interest therein created before January 1, 1924 and then subsisting shall determine, but the person who immediately before the date at which the right would have expired was the owner of the right or interest is entitled at his option either
>         (b)  without any assignment or grant, to continue to reproduce or perform the work in like manner as theretofore subject to the payment, if demanded by the author within three years after the date at which the right would have expired, of such royalties to the author as, failing agreement, may be determined by arbitration, or, where the work is incorporated in a collective work and the owner of the right or interest is the proprietor of that collective work, without any payment,

Section 60 , subsection (3)  of the Canadian "Copyright Act" states:
>     60 (3)  For the purposes of this section, author includes the legal representatives of a deceased author.

Section 60 , subsection (4)  of the Canadian "Copyright Act" states:
>     60 (4)  Subject to this Act, copyright shall not subsist in any work made before January 1, 1924 otherwise than under and in accordance with the provisions of this section.


Section 61  : Clerical Errors / Clerical errors do not invalidate
-----------------------------------------------------------------

Section 61  of the Canadian "Copyright Act" states:
>     Clerical errors in any instrument of record in the Copyright Office do not invalidate the instrument, but they may be corrected under the authority of the Registrar of Copyrights.


Section 62  : Regulations / Regulations
---------------------------------------

Section 62 , subsection (1) , paragraph (a)  of the Canadian "Copyright Act" states:
>     62 (1)  The Governor in Council may make regulations
>         (a)  for the purposes of paragraph 30.01(6)(d), respecting measures, which may vary according to circumstances specified in the regulations;

Section 62 , subsection (1) , paragraph (b)  of the Canadian "Copyright Act" states:
>     62 (1)  The Governor in Council may make regulations
>         (b)  for the purposes of paragraph 30.02(3)(d), respecting measures, which may vary according to circumstances specified in the regulations;

Section 62 , subsection (1) , paragraph (c)  of the Canadian "Copyright Act" states:
>     62 (1)  The Governor in Council may make regulations
>         (c)  prescribing the form of a notice of claimed infringement referred to in section 41.25 and prescribing the information that must be and that is not permitted to be contained in it;

Section 62 , subsection (1) , paragraph (d)  of the Canadian "Copyright Act" states:
>     62 (1)  The Governor in Council may make regulations
>         (d)  prescribing anything that by this Act is to be prescribed by regulation; and

Section 62 , subsection (1) , paragraph (e)  of the Canadian "Copyright Act" states:
>     62 (1)  The Governor in Council may make regulations
>         (e)  generally for carrying out the purposes and provisions of this Act.

Section 62 , subsection (2)  of the Canadian "Copyright Act" states:
>     62 (2)  The Governor in Council may make orders for altering, revoking or varying any order in council made under this Act, but any order made under this section does not affect prejudicially any rights or interests acquired or accrued at the date when the order comes into operation, and shall provide for the protection of those rights and interests.


Section 63  : Industrial Designs and Topographies / 
----------------------------------------------------

Section 63  of the Canadian "Copyright Act", was repealed: [Repealed, 1997, c. 24, s. 38]


Section 64  : Industrial Designs and Topographies / Interpretation
------------------------------------------------------------------

Section 64 , subsection (1)  of the Canadian "Copyright Act" defines "article":
>     64 (1)  In this section and section 64.1,
>         article: article means any thing that is made by hand, tool or machine; (objet)


According to Section 64 , subsection (1)  of the Canadian "Copyright Act", "article" translate to French as "objet".

Section 64 , subsection (1)  of the Canadian "Copyright Act" defines "design":
>     64 (1)  In this section and section 64.1,
>         design: design means features of shape, configuration, pattern or ornament and any combination of those features that, in a finished article, appeal to and are judged solely by the eye; (dessin)


According to Section 64 , subsection (1)  of the Canadian "Copyright Act", "design" translate to French as "dessin".

Section 64 , subsection (1)  of the Canadian "Copyright Act" defines "useful article":
>     64 (1)  In this section and section 64.1,
>         useful article: useful article means an article that has a utilitarian function and includes a model of any such article; (objet utilitaire)


According to Section 64 , subsection (1)  of the Canadian "Copyright Act", "useful article" translate to French as "objet utilitaire".

Section 64 , subsection (1)  of the Canadian "Copyright Act" defines "utilitarian function":
>     64 (1)  In this section and section 64.1,
>         utilitarian function: utilitarian function, in respect of an article, means a function other than merely serving as a substrate or carrier for artistic or literary matter. (fonction utilitaire)


According to Section 64 , subsection (1)  of the Canadian "Copyright Act", "utilitarian function" translate to French as "fonction utilitaire".

Section 64 , subsection (2) , paragraph (a)  of the Canadian "Copyright Act" states:
>     64 (2)  Where copyright subsists in a design applied to a useful article or in an artistic work from which the design is derived and, by or under the authority of any person who owns the copyright in Canada or who owns the copyright elsewhere,
>         (a)  the article is reproduced in a quantity of more than fifty, or

Section 64 , subsection (2) , paragraph (b)  of the Canadian "Copyright Act" states:
>     64 (2)  Where copyright subsists in a design applied to a useful article or in an artistic work from which the design is derived and, by or under the authority of any person who owns the copyright in Canada or who owns the copyright elsewhere,
>         (b)  where the article is a plate, engraving or cast, the article is used for producing more than fifty useful articles,

Section 64 , subsection (2) , paragraph (c)  of the Canadian "Copyright Act" states:
>     64 (2)  Where copyright subsists in a design applied to a useful article or in an artistic work from which the design is derived and, by or under the authority of any person who owns the copyright in Canada or who owns the copyright elsewhere,
>         (c)  to reproduce the design of the article or a design not differing substantially from the design of the article by
>            (i)  making the article, or
>            (ii)  making a drawing or other reproduction in any material form of the article, or

Section 64 , subsection (2) , paragraph (d)  of the Canadian "Copyright Act" states:
>     64 (2)  Where copyright subsists in a design applied to a useful article or in an artistic work from which the design is derived and, by or under the authority of any person who owns the copyright in Canada or who owns the copyright elsewhere,
>         (d)  to do with an article, drawing or reproduction that is made as described in paragraph (c) anything that the owner of the copyright has the sole right to do with the design or artistic work in which the copyright subsists.

Section 64 , subsection (3) , paragraph (a)  of the Canadian "Copyright Act" states:
>     64 (3)  Subsection (2) does not apply in respect of the copyright or the moral rights in an artistic work in so far as the work is used as or for
>         (a)  a graphic or photographic representation that is applied to the face of an article;

Section 64 , subsection (3) , paragraph (b)  of the Canadian "Copyright Act" states:
>     64 (3)  Subsection (2) does not apply in respect of the copyright or the moral rights in an artistic work in so far as the work is used as or for
>         (b)  a trademark or a representation thereof or a label;

Section 64 , subsection (3) , paragraph (c)  of the Canadian "Copyright Act" states:
>     64 (3)  Subsection (2) does not apply in respect of the copyright or the moral rights in an artistic work in so far as the work is used as or for
>         (c)  material that has a woven or knitted pattern or that is suitable for piece goods or surface coverings or for making wearing apparel;

Section 64 , subsection (3) , paragraph (d)  of the Canadian "Copyright Act" states:
>     64 (3)  Subsection (2) does not apply in respect of the copyright or the moral rights in an artistic work in so far as the work is used as or for
>         (d)  an architectural work that is a building or a model of a building;

Section 64 , subsection (3) , paragraph (e)  of the Canadian "Copyright Act" states:
>     64 (3)  Subsection (2) does not apply in respect of the copyright or the moral rights in an artistic work in so far as the work is used as or for
>         (e)  a representation of a real or fictitious being, event or place that is applied to an article as a feature of shape, configuration, pattern or ornament;

Section 64 , subsection (3) , paragraph (f)  of the Canadian "Copyright Act" states:
>     64 (3)  Subsection (2) does not apply in respect of the copyright or the moral rights in an artistic work in so far as the work is used as or for
>         (f)  articles that are sold as a set, unless more than fifty sets are made; or

Section 64 , subsection (3) , paragraph (g)  of the Canadian "Copyright Act" states:
>     64 (3)  Subsection (2) does not apply in respect of the copyright or the moral rights in an artistic work in so far as the work is used as or for
>         (g)  such other work or article as may be prescribed by regulation.

Section 64 , subsection (4)  of the Canadian "Copyright Act" states:
>     64 (4)  Subsections (2) and (3) apply only in respect of designs created after the coming into force of this subsection, and section 64 of this Act and the Industrial Design Act, as they read immediately before the coming into force of this subsection, as well as the rules made under them, continue to apply in respect of designs created before that coming into force.


Section 64.1  : Industrial Designs and Topographies / Non-infringement re useful article features
-------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

Section 64.1 , subsection (1) , paragraph (a)  of the Canadian "Copyright Act" states:
>     64.1 (1)  The following acts do not constitute an infringement of the copyright or moral rights in a work:
>         (a)  applying to a useful article features that are dictated solely by a utilitarian function of the article;

Section 64.1 , subsection (1) , paragraph (b)  of the Canadian "Copyright Act" states:
>     64.1 (1)  The following acts do not constitute an infringement of the copyright or moral rights in a work:
>         (b)  by reference solely to a useful article, making a drawing or other reproduction in any material form of any features of the article that are dictated solely by a utilitarian function of the article;

Section 64.1 , subsection (1) , paragraph (c)  of the Canadian "Copyright Act" states:
>     64.1 (1)  The following acts do not constitute an infringement of the copyright or moral rights in a work:
>         (c)  doing with a useful article having only features described in paragraph (a), or with a drawing or reproduction made as described in paragraph (b), anything that the owner of the copyright has the sole right to do with the work; and

Section 64.1 , subsection (1) , paragraph (d)  of the Canadian "Copyright Act" states:
>     64.1 (1)  The following acts do not constitute an infringement of the copyright or moral rights in a work:
>         (d)  using any method or principle of manufacture or construction.

Section 64.1 , subsection (2) , paragraph (a)  of the Canadian "Copyright Act" states:
>     64.1 (2)  Nothing in subsection (1) affects
>         (a)  the copyright, or

Section 64.1 , subsection (2) , paragraph (b)  of the Canadian "Copyright Act" states:
>     64.1 (2)  Nothing in subsection (1) affects
>         (b)  the moral rights, if any,


Section 64.2  : Industrial Designs and Topographies / Application of Act to topographies
----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

Section 64.2 , subsection (1)  of the Canadian "Copyright Act" states:
>     64.2 (1)  This Act does not apply, and shall be deemed never to have applied, to any topography or to any design, however expressed, that is intended to generate all or part of a topography.

Section 64.2 , subsection (2)  of the Canadian "Copyright Act" states:
>     64.2 (2)  For greater certainty, the incorporation of a computer program into an integrated circuit product or the incorporation of a work into such a computer program may constitute an infringement of the copyright or moral rights in a work.

Section 64.2 , subsection (3)  of the Canadian "Copyright Act" states:
>     64.2 (3)  In this section, “topography” and “integrated circuit product” have the same meaning as in the Integrated Circuit Topography Act.


Section 65  : Industrial Designs and Topographies / 
----------------------------------------------------

Section 65  of the Canadian "Copyright Act", was repealed: [Repealed, 1993, c. 44, s. 69]


Section 66  : Copyright Board / Establishment
---------------------------------------------

Section 66 , subsection (1)  of the Canadian "Copyright Act" states:
>     66 (1)  There is established a Board to be known as the Copyright Board, consisting of not more than five members, including a Chair and a Vice-chair, to be appointed by the Governor in Council.

Section 66 , subsection (2)  of the Canadian "Copyright Act" states:
>     66 (2)  The members of the Board shall be appointed to serve either full-time or part-time.

Section 66 , subsection (3)  of the Canadian "Copyright Act" states:
>     66 (3)  The Chair must be a judge, either sitting or retired, of a superior court.

Section 66 , subsection (4)  of the Canadian "Copyright Act" states:
>     66 (4)  Each member of the Board shall hold office during good behaviour for a term not exceeding five years, but may be removed at any time by the Governor in Council for cause.

Section 66 , subsection (5)  of the Canadian "Copyright Act" states:
>     66 (5)  A member of the Board is eligible to be re-appointed once only.

Section 66 , subsection (6)  of the Canadian "Copyright Act" states:
>     66 (6)  A member of the Board shall not be employed in the public service within the meaning of the Federal Public Sector Labour Relations Act during the member’s term of office.

Section 66 , subsection (7) , paragraph (a)  of the Canadian "Copyright Act" states:
>     66 (7)  A full-time member of the Board, other than the Chair, is deemed to be employed in
>         (a)  the public service for the purposes of the Public Service Superannuation Act; and

Section 66 , subsection (7) , paragraph (b)  of the Canadian "Copyright Act" states:
>     66 (7)  A full-time member of the Board, other than the Chair, is deemed to be employed in
>         (b)  the federal public administration for the purposes of any regulations made pursuant to section 9 of the Aeronautics Act.


Section 66.1  : Copyright Board / Duties of Chair
-------------------------------------------------

Section 66.1 , subsection (1)  of the Canadian "Copyright Act" states:
>     66.1 (1)  The Chair shall direct the work of the Board and apportion its work among its members.

Section 66.1 , subsection (2)  of the Canadian "Copyright Act" states:
>     66.1 (2)  If the Chair is absent or incapacitated or if the office of Chair is vacant, the Vice-chair has all the powers and functions of the Chair during the absence, incapacity or vacancy.

Section 66.1 , subsection (3)  of the Canadian "Copyright Act" states:
>     66.1 (3)  The Vice-chair is the chief executive officer of the Board and has supervision over and direction of the Board and its staff.


Section 66.2  : Copyright Board / Remuneration and expenses
-----------------------------------------------------------

Section 66.2  of the Canadian "Copyright Act" states:
>     The members of the Board shall be paid such remuneration as may be fixed by the Governor in Council and are entitled to be paid reasonable travel and living expenses incurred by them in the course of their duties under this Act while absent from their ordinary place of residence.


Section 66.3  : Copyright Board / Conflict of interest prohibited
-----------------------------------------------------------------

Section 66.3 , subsection (1)  of the Canadian "Copyright Act" states:
>     66.3 (1)  A member of the Board shall not, directly or indirectly, engage in any activity, have any interest in a business or accept or engage in any office or employment that is inconsistent with the member’s duties.

Section 66.3 , subsection (2)  of the Canadian "Copyright Act" states:
>     66.3 (2)  Where a member of the Board becomes aware that he is in a conflict of interest contrary to subsection (1), the member shall, within one hundred and twenty days, terminate the conflict or resign.


Section 66.4  : Copyright Board / Staff
---------------------------------------

Section 66.4 , subsection (1)  of the Canadian "Copyright Act" states:
>     66.4 (1)  Such officers and employees as are necessary for the proper conduct of the work of the Board shall be appointed in accordance with the Public Service Employment Act.

Section 66.4 , subsection (2)  of the Canadian "Copyright Act" states:
>     66.4 (2)  The officers and employees referred to in subsection (1) shall be deemed to be employed in the public service for the purposes of the Public Service Superannuation Act.

Section 66.4 , subsection (3)  of the Canadian "Copyright Act" states:
>     66.4 (3)  The Board may engage on a temporary basis the services of persons having technical or specialized knowledge to advise and assist in the performance of its duties and the Board may, in accordance with Treasury Board directives, fix and pay the remuneration and expenses of those persons.


Section 66.5  : Copyright Board / Concluding matters after membership expires
-----------------------------------------------------------------------------

Section 66.5 , subsection (1)  of the Canadian "Copyright Act" states:
>     66.5 (1)  A member of the Board whose term expires may conclude the matters that the member has begun to consider.

Section 66.5 , subsection (2)  of the Canadian "Copyright Act" states:
>     66.5 (2)  Matters before the Board shall be decided by a majority of the members of the Board and the presiding member shall have a second vote in the case of a tie.


Section 66.501  : Copyright Board / Fair and equitable
------------------------------------------------------

Section 66.501 , paragraph (a)  of the Canadian "Copyright Act" states:
>     66.501  The Board shall fix royalty and levy rates and any related terms and conditions under this Act that are fair and equitable, in consideration of
>         (a)  what would have been agreed upon between a willing buyer and a willing seller acting in a competitive market with all relevant information, at arm’s length and free of external constraints;

Section 66.501 , paragraph (b)  of the Canadian "Copyright Act" states:
>     66.501  The Board shall fix royalty and levy rates and any related terms and conditions under this Act that are fair and equitable, in consideration of
>         (b)  the public interest;

Section 66.501 , paragraph (c)  of the Canadian "Copyright Act" states:
>     66.501  The Board shall fix royalty and levy rates and any related terms and conditions under this Act that are fair and equitable, in consideration of
>         (c)  any regulation made under subsection 66.91(1); and

Section 66.501 , paragraph (d)  of the Canadian "Copyright Act" states:
>     66.501  The Board shall fix royalty and levy rates and any related terms and conditions under this Act that are fair and equitable, in consideration of
>         (d)  any other criterion that the Board considers appropriate.


Section 66.502  : Copyright Board / Informal and expeditious
------------------------------------------------------------

Section 66.502  of the Canadian "Copyright Act" states:
>     All matters before the Board shall be dealt with as informally and expeditiously as the circumstances and considerations of fairness permit but, in any case, within any period or no later than any day provided for under this Act.


Section 66.503  : Copyright Board / For greater certainty
---------------------------------------------------------

Section 66.503  of the Canadian "Copyright Act" states:
>     For greater certainty, any person or entity may authorize any other person or entity to act on their behalf in any matter before the Board.


Section 66.504  : Copyright Board / Case manager
------------------------------------------------

Section 66.504 , subsection (1)  of the Canadian "Copyright Act" states:
>     66.504 (1)  The Chair may assign a member, officer or employee of the Board or a person engaged under subsection 66.4(3) to act as a case manager of a matter before the Board.

Section 66.504 , subsection (2) , paragraph (a)  of the Canadian "Copyright Act" states:
>     66.504 (2)  The case manager may give any directions or make any orders with respect to the case management of the matter, but is not permitted to make a direction or order that is inconsistent with
>         (a)  this Act;

Section 66.504 , subsection (2) , paragraph (b)  of the Canadian "Copyright Act" states:
>     66.504 (2)  The case manager may give any directions or make any orders with respect to the case management of the matter, but is not permitted to make a direction or order that is inconsistent with
>         (b)  regulations made under subsection 66.6(1), unless authorized to do so under regulations made under paragraph 66.6(1.1)(b); or

Section 66.504 , subsection (2) , paragraph (c)  of the Canadian "Copyright Act" states:
>     66.504 (2)  The case manager may give any directions or make any orders with respect to the case management of the matter, but is not permitted to make a direction or order that is inconsistent with
>         (c)  regulations made under paragraph 66.91(2)(a) to (c), unless authorized to do so under regulations made under paragraph 66.91(2)(d).

Section 66.504 , subsection (3)  of the Canadian "Copyright Act" states:
>     66.504 (3)  A direction given, or an order made, by a case manager is deemed to be a direction or order of the Board, including for the purposes of paragraph 28(1)(j) of the Federal Courts Act.

Section 66.504 , subsection (4)  of the Canadian "Copyright Act" states:
>     66.504 (4)  The Chair may delegate his or her power under subsection (1) to the Vice-chair.


Section 66.51  : Copyright Board / Interim decisions
----------------------------------------------------

Section 66.51  of the Canadian "Copyright Act" states:
>     The Board may, on application, make an interim decision.


Section 66.52  : Copyright Board / Variation of decisions
---------------------------------------------------------

Section 66.52  of the Canadian "Copyright Act" states:
>     A decision of the Board respecting royalties or their related terms and conditions that is made under subsection 70(1), 71(2), 76.1(1) or 83(8) may, on application, be varied by the Board if, in its opinion, there has been a material change in circumstances since the decision was made.


Section 66.6  : Copyright Board / Regulations
---------------------------------------------

Section 66.6 , subsection (1) , paragraph (a)  of the Canadian "Copyright Act" states:
>     66.6 (1)  The Board may, with the approval of the Governor in Council, make regulations governing
>         (a)  the practice and procedure in respect of the Board’s hearings, including the number of members of the Board that constitutes a quorum;

Section 66.6 , subsection (1) , paragraph (b)  of the Canadian "Copyright Act" states:
>     66.6 (1)  The Board may, with the approval of the Governor in Council, make regulations governing
>         (b)  the time and manner in which applications and notices must be made or given;

Section 66.6 , subsection (1) , paragraph (c)  of the Canadian "Copyright Act" states:
>     66.6 (1)  The Board may, with the approval of the Governor in Council, make regulations governing
>         (c)  the establishment of forms for the making or giving of applications and notices; and

Section 66.6 , subsection (1) , paragraph (d)  of the Canadian "Copyright Act" states:
>     66.6 (1)  The Board may, with the approval of the Governor in Council, make regulations governing
>         (d)  the carrying out of the work of the Board, the management of its internal affairs and the duties of its officers and employees.

Section 66.6 , subsection (1.1) , paragraph (a)  of the Canadian "Copyright Act" states:
>     66.6 (1.1)  The Board may, with the approval of the Governor in Council, make regulations governing the case management of matters before the Board, including regulations
>         (a)  governing the directions a case manager may give and the orders they may make; and

Section 66.6 , subsection (1.1) , paragraph (b)  of the Canadian "Copyright Act" states:
>     66.6 (1.1)  The Board may, with the approval of the Governor in Council, make regulations governing the case management of matters before the Board, including regulations
>         (b)  authorizing a case manager to give a direction or make an order that adapts, restricts or excludes the application of any provision of regulations made under subsection (1) to a matter or any step in a matter.

Section 66.6 , subsection (2)  of the Canadian "Copyright Act" states:
>     66.6 (2)  A copy of each regulation that the Board proposes to make under subsection (1) or (1.1) shall be published in the Canada Gazette at least 60 days before the regulation’s proposed effective date, and a reasonable opportunity shall be given to interested persons to make representations with respect to the regulation.

Section 66.6 , subsection (3)  of the Canadian "Copyright Act" states:
>     66.6 (3)  No proposed regulation that has been published pursuant to subsection (2) need again be published under that subsection, whether or not it has been altered as a result of representations made with respect thereto.


Section 66.7  : Copyright Board / General powers, etc.
------------------------------------------------------

Section 66.7 , subsection (1)  of the Canadian "Copyright Act" states:
>     66.7 (1)  The Board has, with respect to the attendance, swearing and examination of witnesses, the production and inspection of documents, the enforcement of its decisions and other matters necessary or proper for the due exercise of its jurisdiction, all such powers, rights and privileges as are vested in a superior court of record.

Section 66.7 , subsection (2)  of the Canadian "Copyright Act" states:
>     66.7 (2)  Any decision of the Board may, for the purposes of its enforcement, be made an order of the Federal Court or of any superior court and is enforceable in the same manner as an order thereof.

Section 66.7 , subsection (3)  of the Canadian "Copyright Act" states:
>     66.7 (3)  To make a decision of the Board an order of a court, the usual practice and procedure of the court in such matters may be followed or a certified copy of the decision may be filed with the registrar of the court and thereupon the decision becomes an order of the court.

Section 66.7 , subsection (4)  of the Canadian "Copyright Act" states:
>     66.7 (4)  Where a decision of the Board that has been made an order of a court is varied by a subsequent decision of the Board, the order of the court shall be deemed to have been varied accordingly and the subsequent decision may, in the same manner, be made an order of the court.


Section 66.71  : Copyright Board / Distribution, publication of notices
-----------------------------------------------------------------------

Section 66.71  of the Canadian "Copyright Act" states:
>     Independently of any other provision of this Act relating to the distribution or publication of information or documents by the Board, the Board may at any time cause to be distributed or published, in any manner and on any terms and conditions that it sees fit, any notice that it sees fit to be distributed or published.


Section 66.8  : Copyright Board / Studies
-----------------------------------------

Section 66.8  of the Canadian "Copyright Act" states:
>     The Board shall conduct such studies with respect to the exercise of its powers as are requested by the Minister.


Section 66.9  : Copyright Board / Report
----------------------------------------

Section 66.9 , subsection (1)  of the Canadian "Copyright Act" states:
>     66.9 (1)  The Board shall, not later than August 31 in each year, submit to the Governor in Council through the Minister an annual report on the Board’s activities for the preceding year describing briefly the applications made to the Board, the Board’s decisions and any other matter that the Board considers relevant.

Section 66.9 , subsection (2)  of the Canadian "Copyright Act" states:
>     66.9 (2)  The Minister shall cause a copy of each annual report to be laid before each House of Parliament on any of the first fifteen days on which that House is sitting after the Minister receives the report.


Section 66.91  : Copyright Board / Regulations
----------------------------------------------

Section 66.91 , subsection (1) , paragraph (a)  of the Canadian "Copyright Act" states:
>     66.91 (1)  The Governor in Council may make regulations issuing policy directions to the Board and establishing general criteria to be applied by the Board or to which the Board must have regard
>         (a)  in establishing fair and equitable royalties to be paid pursuant to this Act; and

Section 66.91 , subsection (1) , paragraph (b)  of the Canadian "Copyright Act" states:
>     66.91 (1)  The Governor in Council may make regulations issuing policy directions to the Board and establishing general criteria to be applied by the Board or to which the Board must have regard
>         (b)  in rendering its decisions in any matter within its jurisdiction.

Section 66.91 , subsection (2) , paragraph (a)  of the Canadian "Copyright Act" states:
>     66.91 (2)  The Governor in Council may make regulations
>         (a)  establishing the day by which, or the period within which, a matter before the Board — and any procedural step in the matter, whether set out in a provision of this Act or not — must be completed;

Section 66.91 , subsection (2) , paragraph (b)  of the Canadian "Copyright Act" states:
>     66.91 (2)  The Governor in Council may make regulations
>         (b)  establishing the minimum length of the effective period for the purposes of subsections 68.1(2) and 83(4);

Section 66.91 , subsection (2) , paragraph (c)  of the Canadian "Copyright Act" states:
>     66.91 (2)  The Governor in Council may make regulations
>         (c)  establishing a day for the purposes of paragraph 73.4(b); and

Section 66.91 , subsection (2) , paragraph (d)  of the Canadian "Copyright Act" states:
>     66.91 (2)  The Governor in Council may make regulations
>         (d)  authorizing the Board or a case manager to give a direction or make an order that adapts, restricts or excludes the application of any provision of regulations made under any of paragraphs (a) to (c) to a matter or any step in a matter.

Section 66.91 , subsection (3)  of the Canadian "Copyright Act" states:
>     66.91 (3)  Regulations made under subsection (2) prevail over regulations made under subsection 66.6(1) or (1.1) to the extent of an inconsistency or conflict between them.


Section 67  : Collective Societies / Filing of proposed tariffs
---------------------------------------------------------------

Section 67 , subsection (1)  of the Canadian "Copyright Act" states:
>     67 (1)  A collective society may file a proposed tariff with the Board for the purpose of establishing royalties with respect to rights the collective society administers under section 3, 15, 18, 19 or 21.

Section 67 , subsection (2)  of the Canadian "Copyright Act" states:
>     67 (2)  However, a collective society shall file a proposed tariff with the Board for the purpose of establishing royalties referred to in subsection 29.7(2) or (3) or paragraph 31(2)(d).

Section 67 , subsection (3)  of the Canadian "Copyright Act" states:
>     67 (3)  A collective society may enter into agreements for the purpose of establishing royalties with respect to rights the collective society administers under section 3, 15, 18, 19 or 21, other than royalties referred to in subsection 29.7(2) or (3) or paragraph 31(2)(d).


Section 67.1  : Collective Societies / Designation of collective society — paragraph 19(2)(a)
---------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

Section 67.1  of the Canadian "Copyright Act" states:
>     On application by a collective society, the Board may designate the collective society as the sole collective society authorized to collect all royalties referred to in paragraph 19(2)(a) with respect to a sound recording of a musical work.


Section 67.2  : Collective Societies / Requests regarding repertoire
--------------------------------------------------------------------

Section 67.2  of the Canadian "Copyright Act" states:
>     A collective society shall answer, within a reasonable time, all reasonable requests from any person for information about its repertoire of works, performer’s performances, sound recordings or communication signals.


Section 67.3  : Collective Societies / 
---------------------------------------

Section 67.3  of the Canadian "Copyright Act", was repealed: [Repealed, 1997, c. 24, s. 45]


Section 68  : Proposed Tariffs / Filing
---------------------------------------

Section 68  of the Canadian "Copyright Act" states:
>     A proposed tariff must be filed no later than October 15 of the second calendar year before the calendar year in which the proposed tariff is to take effect or, if a day is established under regulations made under subsection 66.91(2), no later than that day.


Section 68.1  : Proposed Tariffs / Form and content
---------------------------------------------------

Section 68.1 , subsection (1) , paragraph (a)  of the Canadian "Copyright Act" states:
>     68.1 (1)  A proposed tariff must be filed in both official languages and include
>         (a)  the acts to which the tariff is to apply;

Section 68.1 , subsection (1) , paragraph (b)  of the Canadian "Copyright Act" states:
>     68.1 (1)  A proposed tariff must be filed in both official languages and include
>         (b)  the proposed royalty rates and any related terms and conditions; and

Section 68.1 , subsection (1) , paragraph (c)  of the Canadian "Copyright Act" states:
>     68.1 (1)  A proposed tariff must be filed in both official languages and include
>         (c)  the effective period of the proposed tariff.

Section 68.1 , subsection (2)  of the Canadian "Copyright Act" states:
>     68.1 (2)  A proposed tariff’s effective period must be at least three calendar years or, if a minimum period is established under regulations made under subsection 66.91(2), at least that minimum period.


Section 68.2  : Proposed Tariffs / Publication and notification
---------------------------------------------------------------

Section 68.2 , paragraph (a)  of the Canadian "Copyright Act" states:
>     68.2  The Board, in the manner that it sees fit,
>         (a)  shall publish the proposed tariff as well as a notice that any objection to the proposed tariff must be filed within the period set out in subsection 68.3(2); and

Section 68.2 , paragraph (b)  of the Canadian "Copyright Act" states:
>     68.2  The Board, in the manner that it sees fit,
>         (b)  may distribute a notice — or cause it to be distributed or published, on any terms and conditions that the Board sees fit — of the publication of the tariff and of the notice referred to in paragraph (a) to any person affected by the proposed tariff.


Section 68.3  : Proposed Tariffs / Filing of objection
------------------------------------------------------

Section 68.3 , subsection (1) , paragraph (a)  of the Canadian "Copyright Act" states:
>     68.3 (1)  An objection to a proposed tariff may be filed with the Board by
>         (a)  an educational institution, if the proposed tariff is filed for the purpose of collecting royalties referred to in subsection 29.7(2) or (3);

Section 68.3 , subsection (1) , paragraph (b)  of the Canadian "Copyright Act" states:
>     68.3 (1)  An objection to a proposed tariff may be filed with the Board by
>         (b)  a retransmitter, as defined in subsection 31(1), if the proposed tariff is filed for the purpose of collecting royalties referred to in paragraph 31(2)(d); or

Section 68.3 , subsection (1) , paragraph (c)  of the Canadian "Copyright Act" states:
>     68.3 (1)  An objection to a proposed tariff may be filed with the Board by
>         (c)  any user, in any other case.

Section 68.3 , subsection (2)  of the Canadian "Copyright Act" states:
>     68.3 (2)  An objection shall be filed no later than the 30th day after the day on which the Board published the proposed tariff under paragraph 68.2(a) or, if a day is established under the regulations made under subsection 66.91(2), no later than that day.

Section 68.3 , subsection (3)  of the Canadian "Copyright Act" states:
>     68.3 (3)  The Board shall provide a copy of the filed objection to the collective society.


Section 68.4  : Proposed Tariffs / Reply to objection
-----------------------------------------------------

Section 68.4 , subsection (1)  of the Canadian "Copyright Act" states:
>     68.4 (1)  The collective society may file a reply to an objection with the Board.

Section 68.4 , subsection (2)  of the Canadian "Copyright Act" states:
>     68.4 (2)  The Board shall provide a copy of the filed reply to the person or entity that filed the objection.


Section 69  : Withdrawal or Amendment of Proposed Tariff / Request to withdraw or amend
---------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

Section 69 , paragraph (a)  of the Canadian "Copyright Act" states:
>     69  A collective society may, before a proposed tariff filed by it has been approved by the Board, make an application to the Board requesting that
>         (a)  the proposed tariff be withdrawn; or

Section 69 , paragraph (b)  of the Canadian "Copyright Act" states:
>     69  A collective society may, before a proposed tariff filed by it has been approved by the Board, make an application to the Board requesting that
>         (b)  a reference to an act set out in the proposed tariff be excluded from the approved tariff for all of the proposed effective period or, despite subsection 68.1(2), for a portion of that period.


Section 69.1  : Withdrawal or Amendment of Proposed Tariff / Approval by Board
------------------------------------------------------------------------------

Section 69.1 , subsection (1) , paragraph (a)  of the Canadian "Copyright Act" states:
>     69.1 (1)  The Board shall approve an application made under section 69 if it is satisfied that
>         (a)  the collective society has provided sufficient public notice of its intention to make the application;

Section 69.1 , subsection (1) , paragraph (b)  of the Canadian "Copyright Act" states:
>     69.1 (1)  The Board shall approve an application made under section 69 if it is satisfied that
>         (b)  every person who, in respect of the proposed effective period, has paid royalties that would not be payable if the application were approved has
>            (i)  consented to the application,
>            (ii)  received a refund of the royalties, or
>            (iii)  entered into an agreement under subsection 67(3) that covers the act, repertoire or proposed effective period that is the subject of the application; and

Section 69.1 , subsection (1) , paragraph (c)  of the Canadian "Copyright Act" states:
>     69.1 (1)  The Board shall approve an application made under section 69 if it is satisfied that
>         (c)  in the case of an application made under paragraph 69(b) with respect to a portion of the proposed effective period, the application is not made for the purpose of improperly circumventing the required minimum effective period.

Section 69.1 , subsection (2)  of the Canadian "Copyright Act" states:
>     69.1 (2)  For greater certainty, the approval of an application made under section 69 does not preclude the collective society from filing, in accordance with this Act, a proposed tariff that deals in whole or in part with the act, repertoire or proposed effective period that was the subject of the application.


Section 70  : Approval of Tariffs / Approval
--------------------------------------------

Section 70 , subsection (1)  of the Canadian "Copyright Act" states:
>     70 (1)  The Board shall — within the period, if any, that is established under regulations made under subsection 66.91(2) — approve the proposed tariff after making any alterations to the royalty rates and the related terms and conditions, or fixing any new related terms and conditions, that the Board considers appropriate.

Section 70 , subsection (2) , paragraph (a)  of the Canadian "Copyright Act" states:
>     70 (2)  In approving a proposed tariff for the performance in public or the communication to the public by telecommunication of performer’s performances of musical works, or of sound recordings embodying such performer’s performances, the Board shall ensure that
>         (a)  the tariff applies in respect of performer’s performances and sound recordings only in the situations referred to in section 20;

Section 70 , subsection (2) , paragraph (b)  of the Canadian "Copyright Act" states:
>     70 (2)  In approving a proposed tariff for the performance in public or the communication to the public by telecommunication of performer’s performances of musical works, or of sound recordings embodying such performer’s performances, the Board shall ensure that
>         (b)  the tariff does not, because of linguistic and content requirements of Canada’s broadcasting policy set out in section 3 of the Broadcasting Act, place some users that are subject to that Act at a greater financial disadvantage than others; and

Section 70 , subsection (2) , paragraph (c)  of the Canadian "Copyright Act" states:
>     70 (2)  In approving a proposed tariff for the performance in public or the communication to the public by telecommunication of performer’s performances of musical works, or of sound recordings embodying such performer’s performances, the Board shall ensure that
>         (c)  the payment of royalties by users under section 19 will be made in a single payment.

Section 70 , subsection (3) , paragraph (a)  of the Canadian "Copyright Act" states:
>     70 (3)  The Board shall fix a preferential royalty rate for small cable transmission systems in approving a tariff for
>         (a)  the performance in public of musical works or dramatico-musical works, of performer’s performances of such works, or of sound recordings embodying such works; or

Section 70 , subsection (3) , paragraph (b)  of the Canadian "Copyright Act" states:
>     70 (3)  The Board shall fix a preferential royalty rate for small cable transmission systems in approving a tariff for
>         (b)  the communication to the public by telecommunication of musical works or dramatico-musical works, other than as described in subsection 31(2), of performer’s performances of such works, or of sound recordings embodying such works.

Section 70 , subsection (4)  of the Canadian "Copyright Act" states:
>     70 (4)  The Board shall fix a preferential royalty rate for small retransmission systems in approving a tariff for royalties referred to in paragraph 31(2)(d).

Section 70 , subsection (5)  of the Canadian "Copyright Act" states:
>     70 (5)  For greater certainty, the Board may determine, in respect of any tariff that it approves, the portion of the royalties that is to be paid to each collective society.

Section 70 , subsection (6)  of the Canadian "Copyright Act" states:
>     70 (6)  For greater certainty, the Board must not discriminate between owners of copyright on the ground of their nationality or residence in approving a tariff for royalties referred to in subsection 29.7(2) or (3) or paragraph 31(2)(d).

Section 70 , subsection (7)  of the Canadian "Copyright Act" states:
>     70 (7)  The Governor in Council may make regulations defining “small cable transmission system” and “small retransmission system” for the purposes of this section.


Section 70.1  : Approval of Tariffs / Publication of approved tariff
--------------------------------------------------------------------

Section 70.1 , paragraph (a)  of the Canadian "Copyright Act" states:
>     70.1  The Board shall publish the approved tariff in the Canada Gazette and provide a copy of it, together with the reasons for the Board’s decision, to
>         (a)  the collective society that filed the proposed tariff;

Section 70.1 , paragraph (b)  of the Canadian "Copyright Act" states:
>     70.1  The Board shall publish the approved tariff in the Canada Gazette and provide a copy of it, together with the reasons for the Board’s decision, to
>         (b)  every collective society that is authorized to collect royalties under the tariff;

Section 70.1 , paragraph (c)  of the Canadian "Copyright Act" states:
>     70.1  The Board shall publish the approved tariff in the Canada Gazette and provide a copy of it, together with the reasons for the Board’s decision, to
>         (c)  every person or entity that filed an objection under section 68.3; and

Section 70.1 , paragraph (d)  of the Canadian "Copyright Act" states:
>     70.1  The Board shall publish the approved tariff in the Canada Gazette and provide a copy of it, together with the reasons for the Board’s decision, to
>         (d)  any other person or entity that, in the Board’s opinion, ought to receive the copy and reasons.
